Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Agent's Authority to Sell at Any Price and on Credit
Commentary on the agent's authority to sell at any price and on credit, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an agent's authority to sell at a loss or on credit and identify the practical consequences of each view.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa allows the agent to sell at any price and on credit; Sahibayn restrict by custom.

This lesson examines a key disagreement within the Hanafi school: may an agent sell property at a significant loss or on credit without explicit permission? The ruling from the matn states the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, but his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, restrict it. Understanding this dispute helps clarify the role of custom (‘urf) in limiting absolute agency.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
From the matn: the agent's sale is valid whether little or much, and for cash or credit. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa.
The author of the matn presents this as the default ruling.
2
Identify the opposing view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the agent's sale is not valid if there is a gross loss (ghabn fāḥish) that people do not overlook, and it must be for cash (dirhams/dinars). Credit is only allowed if for trade (Abu Yusuf).
3
Follow the opposing proof
The Sahibayn argue that an absolute command is restricted by custom. Since sales are to fulfill needs, they are tied to customary practices. Selling at a gross loss resembles a gift; barter resembles both sale and purchase, so the absolute term 'sale' does not cover them.
This is a rational proof (qiyas) based on customary practice.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa argues that absolute agency operates absolutely in the absence of suspicion. Selling at a loss or for goods is customary in times of urgent need for cash. The transaction is a complete sale from all aspects, as it would break an oath not to sell.
Need justifies deviation from custom.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If an agent sells at a loss or on credit, the sale is valid per Abu Hanifa but invalid per the Sahibayn unless the loss is negligible or it is cash. Fatwa practice often follows the Sahibayn, but later scholars (al-Nasafi, al-Mahbubi) prefer Abu Hanifa's evidence.
Tarjih is divided; the mufti must be aware of both views.

In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he ordered him to sell to these people, it is permissible by consensus, except if it is himself, his minor child, or his slave without debt, then it is not permissible for him to sell to the principal. End quote. It is restricted to the agent because if the executor sold to them for the equivalent value, it is permissible, but if he favored them, it is not permissible even if the favor is small, and the mudarib is like the executor. Likewise in Jami' al-Fusulayn: If the custodian sold the property of the endowment or leased it to someone whose testimony is not accepted for him, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. And in it: If the administrator leased the endowment property to his adult son or his father, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa unless for more than the market rent, like the sale of an executor. And if he leased it to himself, it is permissible if he is good, otherwise not. End quote. And if he had omitted the phrase 'by sale and purchase' it would have been better to include marriage. He said in al-Bazzaziyyah: If he appointed him to marry (someone) and he married his minor daughter, it is not permissible; if an adult or one whose testimony is not accepted for him, it is not permissible according to him, contrary to the two. End quote. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If a father bought the property of his minor son for the equivalent value or more or less to the extent that people overlook (a small difference), the purchase is valid; if it is to an extent not overlooked, it is not valid. Similarly, if he sold his property to his minor son. And the grandfather (father's father) is like the father in his absence, and his executor. As for the ruling of the executor, he is like the father and grandfather when contracting with a stranger. But with himself, the Imam said: It is valid if he is good. Al-Tahawi mentioned Abu Yusuf's statement with him. And Muhammad said: Not valid at all. End quote. The interpretation of 'goodness' is in Wasaaya al-Khaaniyyah. And it is restricted to the contract to exclude the agent for receipt. Al-Hakim said in al-Kafi: If he appointed him to collect a debt owed to him from the agent's father, son, or the son's mukatab, or his slave, and the agent said 'I have collected the debt and it was destroyed' and the claimant denies him, then the agent's word is accepted. If the agent is a slave and says 'I collected from my master or my master's slave and it perished from me,' he is also believed. If the agent is the son of the claimant or the claimed, it is likewise. End quote.
His statement: (And his sale is valid whether little or much, and for cash or credit) meaning according to the Imam. The two said: His sale is not valid for a decrease that people do not overlook, and it is not valid except with dirhams and dinars, because an absolute command is restricted by custom, because actions are for fulfilling needs, so they are restricted by their contexts. The customary practice is selling for the equivalent price and with currency. Hence, the agency for buying coal, ice, and the sacrificial animal is restricted by the time of need: coal in winter, ice in summer, and the sacrificial animal at its time. And because selling at a gross loss is a sale in one respect and a gift in another; similarly, barter is a sale in one respect and a purchase in another, so the absolute name of sale does not cover it. For him (Abu Hanifa) is that absolute agency for sale operates absolutely in places free from suspicion, and selling at a gross loss or for goods is customary in times of severe need for the price and weariness of loss. The matters are disputed according to Abu Hanifa's reported view, and it is a sale from every aspect such that if one swears not to sell, he breaks his oath by it. However, the father and executor do not possess it because their authority is fiduciary and there is no interest in it. Barter is a purchase from every aspect and a sale from every aspect because the definition of each applies. In al-Bazzaziyyah: Fatwa is given according to the view of the two in the case of the agent for whatever is precious or cheap and for any price. End quote. Exception is made from the author's absolute statement for currency exchange, as in al-Khulasa: The agent for selling dinars and dirhams, if he sells for an amount that people do not overlook, it is not valid by consensus. End quote. He (the author) gave absolute permission for credit sale, but it is restricted according to Abu Yusuf to cases where the sale is for trade; if for need, it is not valid, like a woman giving yarn to a man to sell for her, it is for cash sale, and fatwa is given accordingly. And it is restricted to selling at the customary price, for if the term is extended, it is not valid. If he said 'sell for cash' and he sold for cash or on credit, it is valid. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: The fatwa is according to Abu Yusuf's view. If he said 'do not sell except for cash' and he sold on credit, it is not valid. If he said 'sell on credit for a thousand' and he sold for cash for a thousand, it is valid; if he sold for less than a thousand, it is not valid. In al-Khulasa, he then said: If he said 'sell on credit' and he sold for cash, Imam al-Sarakhsi said: The correct view is that it is not valid by consensus. End quote. I say: There is no contradiction between the two branches because the earlier one specified a price for it and this one did not specify. In al-Binaya: It is valid whether the term is customary or not. In Khizanat al-Muftiyyin: He ordered him to sell his slave and he sold on credit; it is valid according to the most correct view if he sold on credit for a term people use for trading; if he extended the term, it is not valid. End quote. This is a correction of the Imam's statement regarding credit and a restriction of it, and it does not contradict the fatwa of al-Faqih because it is regarding selling for little or much, as is clear. In al-Bazzaziyyah: Whoever permits credit only permits it for a customary term; if extended, it is not valid. It is said: It is valid according to him even if the term is long. End quote. So the absolute statement 'even if the term is long' is weak according to him. And likewise.
Water, so there was a naming of the noun from the source; as in al-Sihah and al-Diwan. End of his statement: (In al-Bazzaziyyah: Fatwa is given according to the view of the two, etc.) Al-Ramli said: He mentioned it at the end of the fourth part of the book of Agency. I say: Sheikh Qasim said in his correction on al-Quduri: He preferred the evidence of the Imam, and it is the relied-upon view according to al-Nasafi, or it is the most correct of the sayings and the chosen view according to al-Mahbubi, and al-Mawsili and Sadr al-Shari'ah agreed with him. His statement: (It is restricted according to Abu Yusuf) in the text is according to Abu Hanifa's view, so what is the meaning of restricting it according to Abu Yusuf? His statement: (According to Abu Yusuf) meaning his earlier statement restricting the permissibility of his credit sale to cases of trade, but the author will later interpret it otherwise. His statement: (The most correct is that it is not valid by consensus) perhaps its reasoning is that a credit sale has a higher price than a cash sale, so his intent is the sale at the higher price because the higher price in the property might be more beneficial for him than the lower price immediately due to not needing it now. This is contrary to the first issue because he sold for cash at the price he was ordered to sell on credit, so he obtained it.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the authority of an agent in sale. The main ruling under commentary is from the matn: 'And his (the agent's) sale is valid whether little or much, and for cash or credit.' The commentator explains that this is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree: they hold that the agent's sale is not valid if there is a significant loss that people would not ordinarily overlook, and it is not valid except for cash (dirhams and dinars). Their reasoning is that absolute commands are restricted by custom ('urf). Since sales are meant to fulfill needs, they are tied to customary practices. Selling at a gross loss resembles a gift, and barter resembles both sale and purchase, so the absolute term 'sale' does not cover them. Abu Hanifa argues that absolute agency operates freely in the absence of suspicion, and selling at a loss or for goods is customary when there is urgent need for cash. He considers such a transaction a complete sale from all aspects. The passage then discusses practical applications: the executor (wasi) and mudarib have restrictions similar to the agent. There is also discussion of credit sales: Abu Yusuf restricts credit sales to cases where the principal is engaged in trade, while Abu Hanifa allows it absolutely, though later authorities qualify it to customary credit terms. The fatwa according to al-Bazzaziyyah is given according to the two companions (Sahibayn), but many later scholars (al-Nasafi, al-Mahbubi, al-Mawsili, Sadr al-Shari'ah) prefer Abu Hanifa's evidence. The passage concludes with a note on the permissibility of selling on credit for a longer term: the correct view is that it is not valid by consensus if the principal specified a cash price and the agent sold on credit at the same price, but if no price was specified then it is valid.

Key Terms
الوكيل (al-wakīl): The agent appointed by the principal (al-muwakkil) to perform a legal act on his behalf.
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghabn al-fāḥish): A significant loss in a sale that people would not ordinarily overlook (i.e., more than customary tolerance).
النسيئة (al-nasī’ah): A credit sale where payment is deferred to a future date.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when is an agent's sale not valid?
A) When it is for cash payment.
B) When there is a significant loss that people do not overlook.
C) When it is on credit with a customary term.
D) When the agent is a relative of the principal.

Key Takeaway
The agent's authority to sell at a loss or on credit is disputed within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa validates it absolutely, while the Sahibayn restrict it by custom, with fatwa practice often following the latter view.

Agent's Authority to Sell with Gross Deficiency or Barter
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agent's sale with ghaban fahish and muqayadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an agent's authority to sell with ghaban fahish or muqayadah, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
An agent may sell for any price; the later fatwa overrides Abu Hanifa's strict view.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the limits of an agent's authority. While Abu Hanifa restricted the absolute permission to sell, his two disciples allowed it even in cases of gross deficiency or barter. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school resolves tensions between textual absoluteness and practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the issue
The act is an agent selling the principal's property. The issue is whether the agent can sell at a gross deficiency (ghaban fahish) or through barter (muqayadah) without explicit permission.
Ghaban fahish means a price significantly below market value; muqayadah is a barter exchange.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that such transactions are not covered by the absolute term 'sale' because they are composites: ghaban fahish mixes sale with gift, and muqayadah mixes sale with purchase. Hence, the agent cannot validly execute them.
His reasoning is based on linguistic precision (haqiqah vs. majaz).
3
Present the disciples' (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) position
The two disciples consider these transactions as valid sales because they meet the definition of sale: exchange of property for property. The absolute agency includes them unless there is a specific prohibition.
They focus on the transactional reality rather than the linguistic classification.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the agent sells with ghaban fahish or barters, the sale is valid according to the disciples but void according to Abu Hanifa.
This difference affects whether the principal can revoke the transaction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and exceptions
According to al-Bazzaziyya, fatwa is given on the disciples' view: the agent may sell for any price, whether cheap or dear. An exception is currency exchange (sarf), where even slight deviation is prohibited by consensus.
The exception shows that general permissibility does not apply to ribawi transactions.

الجمد بالصيف، وفي الأضحية ،بزمانها، ولأن البيع بغبن فاحش بيع من وجه هبة من وجه، وكذا المقايضة بيع من وجه شراء من وجه فلا يتناوله مطلق اسم البيع. وله أن التوكيل بالبيع مطلق فيجري على إطلاقه في غير موضع التهمة، والبيع بالغبن الفاحش أو بالعين متعارف عند شدة الحاجة إلى الثمن والتبرم من الغبن أي الملال والمسائل ممنوعة على قول أبي حنيفة على ما هو المروي عنه، وأنه بيع من كل وجه حتى إن حلف لا يبيع يحنث به غير أن الأب لأن ولايتهما نظرية ولا نظر فيه والمقايضة شراء من كل وجه والوصي لا يملكانه أنه مع بيع بيع وبيع من كل وجه لوجود حد كل واحد منهما. وفي البزازية : ويفتى بقولهما في مسألة الوكيل بما عَزَّ وهان وبأي ثمن كان ا هـ ويستثنى من إطلاق المؤلف الصرف لما في الخلاصة : الوكيل ببيع الدينار والدرهم إذا باع بما لا يتغابن الناس فيه لا يجوز إجماعاً ا هـ .
The ice in summer, and in the sacrifice, in its time, and because the sale with gross deficiency is a sale from one aspect and a gift from another, and similarly barter is a sale from one aspect and a purchase from another, so the absolute term of sale does not include it. And there is that agency for sale is absolute, so it operates according to its absoluteness in a place not of accusation, and sale with gross deficiency or for cash is customary when there is severe need for the price and vexation from the deficiency, meaning boredom, and the cases are prevented according to Abu Hanifa as narrated from him, and that it is a sale from every aspect such that if he swears not to sell, he violates by it, except that the father because their guardianship is theoretical and there is no consideration in it, and barter is a purchase from every aspect and the executor does not own it because it is with a sale a sale and a sale from every aspect due to the existence of the definition of each one. And in al-Bazzaziyya: And fatwa is given according to their saying in the matter of the agent whether cheap or dear and by any price. And an exception is made from the author's absolute statement regarding currency exchange because in al-Khulasa: The agent for selling a dinar and dirham, if he sells for a price not within the range of mutual neglect, it is not allowed by consensus.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on an agent selling property with a gross deficiency (ghaban fahish) or through barter (muqayadah). According to Abu Hanifa, such a sale is not valid because it is partly a gift or partly a purchase, and the absolute term of sale does not cover it. However, it is permitted if it is customary or there is urgency. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow it, and the fatwa follows their view. An exception is currency exchange, where even slight deviation is not allowed by consensus. The passage is from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the limits of agency.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghaban al-fahish): A sale where the price is significantly below the market value, to the extent that it is not normally tolerated among traders.
المقايضة (al-muqayadah): A barter transaction where goods are exchanged for goods instead of currency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa in the Hanafi school, can an agent sell the principal's property at a price significantly below market value (ghaban fahish)?
A) No, because it is not a valid sale.
B) Yes, the agent may sell for any price, whether cheap or dear.
C) Yes, but only for currency exchange.
D) No, except in cases of extreme necessity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's operative fatwa allows an agent to sell with gross deficiency or barter, overriding Abu Hanifa's stricter view.

Agent Selling on Credit: Restrictions and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agent selling on credit with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which an agent may sell on credit according to the Hanafi school, and identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
An agent may sell on credit only for trade with customary terms; deviation invalidates the sale.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the agency contract specifically regarding credit sales. While an absolute agency might seem to permit any sale, the Hanafi school restricts the agent's authority to protect the principal's interest. The ruling differs among the founding imams, and the fatwa follows Abu Yusuf's restrictive view. Understanding these conditions is crucial for valid transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is the agent authorized to do? The act is selling the principal's property. The mode (cash or credit) is at issue. Determine the default ruling: can the agent sell on credit without explicit instruction?
2
Locate the restrictive conditions
According to Abu Yusuf, what conditions must be met for a credit sale to be valid? (1) The sale must be for the purpose of trade (tijarah), not for personal need (hajah). (2) The credit term must be customary (mut'arraf) in the market. If the term is unusually long, it is not allowed.
Restriction is based on protecting the principal's interest.
3
Compare the positions of the Hanafi imams
Abu Hanifa allows the agent to sell on credit even for long terms, unless the principal explicitly prohibits it. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani impose the restrictions. Note that the text says the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view.
Muhammad agrees with Abu Yusuf in substance.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence of the dispute? If an agent sells on credit for a long term (e.g., two years where the norm is one month), according to Abu Hanifa the sale is valid; according to Abu Yusuf it is invalid. The mufta bihi follows Abu Yusuf, so the sale would be invalid.
This highlights how ikhtilaf affects real transactions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Abu Yusuf's restriction. Later authorities like al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, al-Bazzaziyya, and al-Ramli affirm this. The reason is that it safeguards the principal and aligns with market custom.
The permissive view is considered weak.

And he made absolute in the permissibility of his selling on credit, and it is restricted according to Abu Yusuf to when it is for trade; if it is for need, it is not allowed, like a woman who gives yarn to a man to sell for her, so it is for sale for cash, and by it fatwa is given. And restricted to when he sells as people sell, for if the period is long, it is not allowed. And if he said 'Sell for cash' and he sold for cash or on credit, it is allowed. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: And the fatwa is on the saying of Abu Yusuf. And if he said 'Do not sell except for cash' and he sold on credit, it is not allowed. And if he said 'Sell on credit for a thousand' and he sold for cash for a thousand, it is allowed; if he sold for less than a thousand, it is not allowed. In al-Khulasa, then he said: If he said 'Sell on a term' and he sold for cash, Imam al-Sarakhsi said: The most correct is that it is not allowed by consensus. And in al-Binaya: It is allowed for a customary term or otherwise. And in Khizanat al-Muftiyyin: He ordered him to sell his slave, so he sold on credit; it is allowed on the most correct view if he sold on credit as people transact; but if he lengthened the period, it is not allowed. And it is a correction of the Imam's saying regarding credit and a restriction for it, and it does not contradict the fatwa of the faqih because it is regarding selling for little or much, as is not hidden. And in al-Bazzaziyya: And whoever permits credit, only permits it with a customary term; if he lengthens, it is not allowed; and it is said that it is allowed with him even if the period is long. So the absolute statement 'even if the period is long' is weak with him. His saying: (And it is restricted according to Abu Yusuf) what is in the text according to Abu Hanifa, so what is the meaning of restricting it by the saying of Abu Yusuf? His saying: (According to Abu Yusuf) i.e., his previous saying restricting the permissibility of his selling on credit to when it is for trade, but the author will later carry it to other than that. His saying: (The most correct that it is not allowed by consensus) perhaps its reasoning is that sale on credit has a price greater than the price of cash sale, so his intention is the sale at the higher price because the higher price may be more beneficial for him in the property than the lower price immediately due to not needing it now, and this is different from the first case because he sold for cash at the price he ordered him to sell on credit, so he obtained for cash or credit and restricted his purchase to the like of the value and an increase within the range of mutual neglect, which is what enters
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the ruling of an agent selling on credit (nasi'ah). According to Abu Yusuf, the agent may sell on credit only if it is for trade (tijarah); if for personal need (hajah), it must be for cash. The fatwa generally follows Abu Yusuf. Other restrictions include that the credit term should be customary; lengthened terms are not allowed. There is a dispute about whether selling for cash when ordered to sell on credit is valid. Imam al-Sarakhsi says it is not allowed by consensus, but the author reconciles different cases. Al-Binaya allows even non-customary terms. The correct view is that the agent must adhere to customary practices. Later commentators like al-Ramli discuss the differences and preferences.

Key Terms
النسيئة (al-nasi'ah): Sale on credit, where payment is deferred to a future date.
متعارف (mut'arraf): Customary or commonly accepted in market practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa stated by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, when can an agent sell on credit?
A) Only if the principal explicitly permitted it.
B) Only if the sale is for trade and the term is customary.
C) At any time, because agency is absolute.
D) Only if the principal is in need of cash.

Key Takeaway
An agent selling on credit must adhere to customary trade terms; otherwise the sale is invalid per the operative Hanafi view.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
The Agent's Restriction to Fair Value and Definition of Minor Ghabn
Commentary on agent's purchase restriction and definition of minor ghabn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that an agent's purchase is restricted to the like of value plus minor ghabn, define minor ghabn, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two companions regarding deferment and small pledges.

Core Idea
An agent must purchase at fair value; minor ghabn (within assessors' estimates) is tolerated, but excessive ghabn invalidates.

In the Hanafi school, an agent (wakil) is bound to act in the principal's interest. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the agent's purchase must be at the like of value or with an increase that people mutually overlook—the definition of minor ghabn (ghabn yasir). The text then brings various rulings from authoritative Hanafi works, including internal disagreements between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding the agent's authority to grant deferment and to accept a small pledge. Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly assessing the validity of an agent's transaction.

Guided Path
1
State the main condition
Identify the core ruling: the agent's purchase is restricted to the like of the value plus an increase that people mutually overlook (i.e., minor ghabn).
The phrase 'مثل القيمة وزيادة يتغابن الناس فيها' is the key.
2
Define minor ghabn
The text defines minor ghabn as what falls under the estimation of the assessors (تحت تقويم المقومين) – the range of differing expert valuations. There is no fixed percentage.
Ghabn yasir is determined by custom and valuation experts.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on deferment
If the principal authorizes sale on credit without specifying a term, Abu Hanifa allows the agent to set any term absolutely; the two companions restrict it to the customary term.
This dispute appears in the passage from al-Tatimma.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on a small pledge
If the principal orders the agent to sell and take a pledge, Abu Hanifa permits taking even a small pledge; the companions require the pledge to be within the range of minor ghabn (i.e., not negligible).
Source: al-Munya. The key phrase is 'لا إلا فيما يتغابن فيه'.
5
Apply the rule to a case of excessive ghabn
If the agent buys at a price clearly above the assessed value (exceeding the range of assessors), the purchase is invalid (لم يجز). The agent is liable for the excess.
Examples from the text: selling for less than specified price invalidates; selling for more of the same type validates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة باب الوكالة بالبيع والشراء

وبالنقد أو النسيئة وتقيد شراؤه بمثل القيمة وزيادة يتغابن الناس فيها وهو ما يدخل
وكله
الخانية من فصل إجارة الوقف المتولي إذا أجر الوقف بشيء من العروض والحيوان بعينه قيل بأنه يجوز بلا خلاف بخلاف بيع الوكيل وكذا الوكيل بالإجارة إذا أجر بمكيل أو موزون أو عروض أو حيوان قيل بأنه يجوز بلا خلاف قال الفقيه أبو جعفر في زماننا الإجارة تكون على الخلاف أيضاً لأن المتعارف الإجارة بالدراهم والدنانير ا هـ. وفي الخلاصة : : الوكيل بالطلاق والعتاق على مال على الخلاف ا هـ . ومحل الاختلاف عند عدم التعيين من الآمر فإن عين شيئاً تعين إلا فيما قدمناه من تعيين النسيئة مع بيان الثمن فباع حالاً فإنه يجوز، وتقدم لو عين له النقد إثباتاً أو نفياً. وفي الحاوي القدسي : وإن أمره أن يبيعه بشيء معين فباعه بغيره أو بأقل منه لم يجز في قولهم، وإن باعه بأكثر منه من ذلك الجنس جاز ا هـ. وفي كافي الحاكم : فإن باعه بيعاً فاسداً ودفعه لم يكن مخالفاً، ولو قال بعه نسيئة فباعه إلى القطاف أو الحصاد أو النيروز فالبيع فاسد إلا أن يقول المشتري أنا أعجل المال وأدع الأجل فيجوز، ولو طعام فقال ببيع بعه كل کر بخمسين فباعه كله فهو جائز، وإن قال بعه بمثل ما باع به فلان الكر فقال فلان بعت الكر بأربعين فباع ذلك ثم وجد فلان باع بخمسين فالبيع مردود، فإن كان فلان قد باع كراً بخمسين وباع هذا طعامه بخمسين خمسين ثم باع فلان بعد ذلك بستين فذلك جائز ولا ضمان على الوكيل، فإن كان باع كراً بأربعين وكراً بخمسين فباع الوكيل طعامه كله بأربعين أربعين أجزأه استحساناً ا هـ . وفي البزازية : وكله أن يبيع بألف وقيمته كذلك ثم زادت قيمته إلى ألفين لا يملك بيعه بألف باعه بالخيار ثلاثة أيام فزادت قيمته في المدة له أن يجيز عنده لأنه يملك الابتداء فيملك الإمضاء أيضاً، وإن سكت حتى مضت المدة بطل البيع عند محمد خلافاً للثاني ، وكله ببيع عبده بمائة دينار فباعه بألف وقال بعت عبدك ولم يذكر ما باع به ولم يعلم به الموكل فقال أجزت جاز بألف ا هـ . الحاوي القدسي : وإن وكل رجلاً ببيع عبد فباعه فضولي فأجاز الوكيل جاز ا هـ. التتمة : الوكيل بالقسمة لا يملكها بغبن فاحش والتوكيل بالتأجيل في الثمن مطلقاً حتى لو أجله شهراً أو سنة أو سنتين يجوز عند أبي حنيفة على الإطلاق، وعندهما ينصرف إلى المتعارف ا هـ . وفي منية المفتي: قال له بع وخذ رهناً فأخذ رهناً قليلاً جاز عند الإمام،
وعندهما لا إلا فيما يتغابن فيه ا هـ .

Book of Agency, Chapter of Agency for Sale and Purchase. And with cash or credit, and his purchase is restricted to the like of the value and an increase that people mutually overlook, which is what enters under the estimation of the assessors. He appointed him... (full text as per Arabic)

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the restriction of the agent's purchase. It begins by stating the condition that the agent's purchase must be at the like of the value or with an increase that people normally tolerate (ghabn yasir). This is defined as what falls within the range of differing assessments of valuators. The text then brings various rulings from different Hanafi works. It discusses cases where the principal specifies a particular price or term (cash/credit) and the agent deviates. For example, if the principal told him to sell for a specific item and he sold for another or for less, it is not valid; but if he sold for more of the same type, it is valid. It also covers cases of invalid sales, conditional sales, and the effect of changes in market value. The passage includes differences between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding the agent's authority to grant deferment (ta'jil) absolutely or limited to custom, and regarding taking a small pledge. The relied-upon positions are noted from various authoritative sources.

Key Terms
الغبن (al-ghabn): An imbalance in value where one party pays more (or receives less) than the fair value; ghabn yasir is minor and tolerated, ghabn fahish is excessive and invalidates the transaction for certain agents.
الوكيل (al-wakīl): An agent authorized by another (the principal) to perform a specific legal act on their behalf, such as sale or purchase.
النسيئة (al-nasī’ah): Sale on credit with a deferred payment term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of 'ghabn yasir' (minor fraud) that is tolerated in the agent's transaction?
A) Any increase up to 10% of the market value
B) What enters under the estimation of the assessors (under تقويم المقومين)
C) Any amount less than one dirham
D) Whatever the principal later approves

Key Takeaway
The agent's purchase is valid only if the price is at the like of value or includes only a minor ghabn (within assessors' estimates); excessive ghabn invalidates the transaction, and internal Hanafi disputes on deferment and small pledges require careful attention.

Classification of Ghabn Fahish for Different Types of Agents
Detailed commentary on the matn about restricting agent's purchase to fair value, followed by a classification of agents regarding ghabn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify different types of agents (father, executor, mudarib, etc.) according to whether they may buy or sell with ghabn fahish and state the ruling for each category with supporting evidence.

Core Idea
The toleration of ghabn fahish in agency depends on the type of agent and the nature of the transaction; some agents are strictly bound to fair price, others have full discretion.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq concerning the restriction of an agent's purchase to the fair value. It then presents a comprehensive classification from Munyat al-Mufti listing the different categories of agents and the rules of ghabn for each. Understanding this classification is essential for determining the validity of transactions carried out by agents and fiduciaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn phrase and its rule
The commentary begins with the matn phrase 'وتقيد شراؤه بمثل القيمة...' which establishes that an agent's purchase is restricted to the fair value. Note that selling is treated differently.
This is the base rule for a general agent.
2
Analyze the ikhtilaf on agent buying a specific item
When the agent is authorized to buy a specific item, the text presents two views: one that the sale is not effective for the principal (majority) and another that it is effective. Understand the basis of each argument.
The ikhtilaf is noted as unresolved ('لا نص فيه').
3
Extract the comprehensive classification from Munyat al-Mufti
List each type of agent mentioned (father, grandfather, executor, mutawalli, free man, mukatab, slave, mudarib, partners, absolute agent, sick person, etc.) and their corresponding ruling regarding ghabn.
Pay attention to the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions.
4
Note the exception for items with known prices
For items like bread, meat, bananas, cheese, no ghabn is excused even if very small. This overrides the general classifications.
This is a mufta bihi position.
5
Summarize the principles from Jami' al-Fusulayn
The passage ends with a summary categorizing agents into those who tolerate minor ghabn only, those who tolerate both, and those who tolerate none. Understand the logic behind each category.
This summary is a useful mnemonic.

وما لا فلا.

His saying: 'and his purchase is restricted to the like of the value and an increase that people overlook, which is what enters under the estimation of the assessors'. (full text as per Arabic)
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is the direct commentary on the matn phrase 'وتقيد شراؤه بمثل القيمة وزيادة يتغابن الناس فيها وهو ما يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين'. It begins by explaining that if the agent is authorized to sell a slave and sells half, it is valid, but in purchase, he must not buy from the assessors due to suspicion of self-dealing. It then discusses the ruling when the agent is authorized to buy a specific item: according to the sharh (author of al-Hidaya) he cannot buy with excessive ghabn even though he cannot buy for himself, because by violating instructions he becomes a buyer for himself. However, al-Hidaya states that general mashayikh say it is effective for the principal because he cannot buy it for himself. There is a difference of opinion. Then it mentions that for items with widely known prices like bread, meat, bananas, cheese, no ghabn is excused even if very small. The text then quotes from Munyat al-Mufti a comprehensive classification of different types of agents (father, grandfather, executor, trustee of waqf, free man, mukatib, mudarib, etc.) and the rules of ghabn for each: some are restricted to minor ghabn, some can sell with excessive ghabn, and some cannot tolerate any ghabn. It concludes with a summary from Jami' al-Fusulayn and a note from al-Dhakhira about selling on credit vs cash.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghabn al-fāḥish): Excessive imbalance in value beyond what people normally tolerate; it invalidates certain transactions.
المتولي (al-mutawallī): The administrator or trustee of a waqf (endowment).
المضارب (al-muḍārib): The agent in a qirad/mudaraba partnership who manages capital.
الوصي (al-waṣī): The executor of a deceased person's will, often guardian of orphans.
شريك العنان والمفاوض (sharīk al-ʿinān wa al-mufāwaḍa): Partners in a limited (inan) or unlimited (mufawada) partnership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The agent authorized to sell absolutely (الوكيل بالبيع المطلق)
B) The executor of a deceased person (الوصي) when selling to orphans
C) The mudarib (المضارب) when selling
D) The free man (الحر) acting as an agent

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of ghabn fahish in agency transactions depends on the agent's role and the nature of the transaction; this classification is essential for determining the validity of sales and purchases by fiduciaries.

Defining Ghabn Fahish and Yasir in Agency
Defining ghabn and its types with examples and a dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ghabn fahish and ghabn yasir, apply the criterion of arbitrators' evaluation, and state the Hanafi rulings on two controversial cases: agent buying a specific item and well-known priced items.

Core Idea
Ghabn fahish invalidates the agent's purchase; for known-price items, even a penny's deviation is never excused.

Ghabn (disparity) is central to agency law: an agent must not overpay or undersell beyond normal market fluctuation. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies when a difference in price is 'gross' (fahish) and when it is 'slight' (yasir), using the benchmark of arbitrators' evaluation. Two specific scenarios sharpen the rule: an agent buying a unique item, and transactions involving staple goods with transparent prices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the benchmark for ghabn
The text states ghabn is measured by taqwim al-muqawwimin (arbitrators' evaluation). Any price within their range is yasir (excused); outside is fahish (not excused).
This is a procedural test, not a fixed percentage.
2
Analyze the dispute on specific-item purchase
If an agent is appointed to buy a specific thing (e.g., a particular slave) and buys it with ghabn fahish, two views exist: al-Hidayah says it binds the principal because the agent cannot buy it for himself; others say it does not, because suspicion of self-dealing persists. Identify the thamarah (practical difference).
The majority (عامة المشايخ) support the first view.
3
Apply the flat rule for well-known priced items
For items with a common, stable market price (bread, meat, bananas, cheese), no ghabn is excused — even one dirham. This is the muftā bihi (operative fatwa).
The reasoning: such items have no hidden price variation, so any deviation is intentional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تحت تقويم المقومين ولو وكل ببيع عبد فباع نصفه صح وفي الشراء يتوقف ما لم يشتر المقومين لأن التهمة فيه متحققة فلعله اشتراه لنفسه فإذا لم يوافقه ألحقه بغيره على ما مر . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان وكيلاً بشراء شيء بعينه فلا يملك الشراء بغبن فاحش وإن كان لا يملك الشراء لنفسه لأنه بالمخالفة يكون مشترياً لنفسه فكانت التهمة باقية كما ذكره الشارح، وفي الهداية خلافه فإنه قال : حتى لو كان وكيلاً بشراء شيء بعينه قالوا ينفذ على الأمر لأنه لا يملك شراءه لنفسه ا هـ . وذكر في البناية أن ما في الهداية قول عامة المشايخ وبعضهم قال لا ينفذ على الآمر ا هـ . وفي المعراج معزياً إلى الذخيرة أنه لا نص فيه، وشمل ما كان سعره معلوماً شائعاً وهو ضعيف قالوا ما كان معروفاً كالخبز واللحم والموز والجبن لا يعفى فيه الغبن وإن قل ولو كان فلساً واحداً هكذا جزم به الشارح، وفي بيوع التتمة وبه يفتى؛ كذا في البناية.
Under the evaluation of the arbitrators: If he appoints an agent to sell a slave and he sells half of it, it is valid. In purchase, it is suspended until the arbitrators purchase it, because suspicion exists; perhaps he bought it for himself, and if he does not agree, he attributes it to another as previously mentioned. It is general and includes when he is an agent for buying a specific thing; then he does not have the right to buy with gross disparity (ghabn fahish) even if he cannot buy it for himself because by violating the agency he becomes a buyer for himself, so suspicion remains as the commentator mentioned. In al-Hidayah there is a difference: he said: 'Even if he is an agent for buying a specific thing, they said it is binding on the principal because he cannot buy it for himself.' In al-Binaya it is mentioned that what is in al-Hidayah is the view of the majority of scholars, and some said it is not binding on the principal. In al-Mi'raj citing al-Dhakhira, there is no text on it. It includes what has a well-known prevalent price, and this is weak. They said: what is known like bread, meat, bananas, and cheese, ghabn is not excused in it even if little, even if one dirham. Thus the commentator asserted it, and in Buyu' al-Tatimmah it is the fatwa; thus in al-Binaya.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage defines ghabn (disparity) and its two degrees: yasir (slight) and fahish (gross). The criterion is the evaluation of arbitrators (taqwim al-muqawwimin). If the price falls within their evaluation, it is yasir and excused; otherwise it is fahish and not excused. The text then discusses a dispute: when an agent is appointed to buy a specific thing, can he buy it with ghabn fahish? According to al-Hidayah, the purchase binds the principal because the agent cannot buy that specific item for himself. Others disagree, saying the agent remains under suspicion. The passage then clarifies that for items with well-known, stable prices (like bread, meat, bananas, cheese), no ghabn is excused at all, even a single dirham. This is the relied-upon fatwa. The teacher should note that this rule protects the principal when the market price is transparent.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): Gross disparity in price that exceeds what evaluators would consider within normal range.
تقويم المقومين (taqwim al-muqawwimin): The evaluation made by appraisers (arbitrators) to determine a fair price.
غبن يسير (ghabn yasir): Slight disparity within the range of arbitrators' evaluation, excused in agency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The percentage of the price difference (e.g., 5%).
B) The evaluation of arbitrators (muqawwimin).
C) The personal opinion of the principal.
D) The type of item (moveable or immovable).

Key Takeaway
Ghabn is assessed by arbitrators; for known-price items no deviation is excused; for specific items a dispute exists but the majority binds the principal.

Categories of Agents and Ghabn Rulings in Hanafi Fiqh
Classifying agents and their ghabn rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify various types of legal agents (guardians, partners, agents) into three categories based on whether slight or gross ghabn is excused in their transactions, and state the ruling for each category.

Core Idea
Ghabn rulings depend on the agent's role: some agents are only trusted with slight disparity, others with any disparity, and some with none.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of a transaction involving a disparity (ghabn) between price and value depends on the capacity of the transactor. Munyat al-Mufti provides a comprehensive classification of agents and their rulings, distinguishing between slight and gross ghabn. This lesson will help you navigate this classification so you can apply the correct ruling to each type of agent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agent type
First, list all transactors mentioned: father, grandfather, executor, waqf administrator, free person, mukatab, slave (madhun), mudarib, partners (inan, mufawada), agents for sale/purchase, sick debtor, etc.
Note that some agents have different rulings for buying vs. selling.
2
Determine the applicable ghabn ruling
For each agent, extract from the text whether slight ghabn is excused, gross ghabn is excused, both, or neither. For example, the father is only allowed slight ghabn, while the agent for sale is allowed both.
Pay attention to intra-Hanafi differences (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn).
3
Categorize into one of three groups
The text summarizes three categories: (1) only slight ghabn is excused, (2) both slight and gross are excused, (3) neither slight nor gross is excused. Place each agent in the appropriate category.
The summary is the key takeaway.
4
Apply to hypothetical scenarios
Practice with examples: A father sells his child's property with a 10% disparity. Is it valid? An agent for sale sells with a 20% disparity. Valid? Use the classification to answer.
Remember that custom ('urf) defines what is slight vs. gross.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

In Munyat al-Mufti: Categories of transactors: The transaction of the father, grandfather, executor, and administrator of a waqf is only valid with a fair price or with slight ghabn. The transaction of a free person is valid in any case, similarly a mukatab and a slave given permission according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: restricted to a fair price. For the mudarib, partner of 'inan, partner of mufawada, and agent for absolute sale, selling with gross ghabn is permissible, and their purchase with it is against them. The sick debtor whose debt covers his entire wealth cannot sell with slight ghabn, but his executor can sell with it to pay his debt. The sale by a sick person to his heir is invalid absolutely according to Abu Hanifa; according to them (Sahibayn), it is valid for its value or more. The sale by a debtor to his master with slight ghabn is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. The sale and purchase of an executor from an orphan is not valid unless it is beneficial for the orphan according to Abu Hanifa; according to them, it is absolutely invalid. Summary of ghabn issues: Among them are cases where slight ghabn is excused but not gross: the transaction of father, grandfather, executor, administrator, mudarib, and agent for buying something not specified. Cases where both slight and gross ghabn are excused: the transaction of an agent for sale, agent for buying a specific thing, a minor given permission, a slave given permission, a mukatab, partner of 'inan, and partner of mufawada. Cases where neither slight nor gross ghabn is excused: the transaction of an agent for sale from someone whose testimony is accepted, the sale by the owner of capital of mudaraba funds, the usurper who compensates by value with an oath and then the item appears with greater value, when someone bequeaths one-third of his wealth and acts during his death illness with ghabn (it is from the third even if slight), the transaction of a debtor whose debt is overwhelming, and the sale by a sick person to his heir. Its completion is in Jami' al-Fusulayn. It is restricted to purchase because the agent for marriage, if he gives him in marriage for more than her dower equivalent, it is invalid. Then I saw in al-Dhakhira: If he appoints him to sell on credit and he sells for cash, if he sells for cash at the price it is sold on credit, it is valid; otherwise not.

This passage from Munyat al-Mufti provides a comprehensive classification of various types of agents and their rulings regarding ghabn. It first lists the categories of agents and their specific rules. Then a summary (حاصل) divides all cases into three groups: (1) only slight ghabn is excused, (2) both slight and gross are excused, and (3) neither is excused. This summary is the key takeaway. The passage also includes an additional note from al-Dhakhira regarding an agent appointed for credit sale but selling for cash. The teacher should emphasize that the classification is based on the level of trust and potential harm to the principal.

Key Terms
غبن يسير (ghabn yasir): Slight disparity that is typically tolerated in transactions.
مضارب (mudarib): A working partner in a mudaraba (profit-sharing) contract.
وكيل بالبيع (wakil bi al-bay'): An agent authorized to sell.
المديون المستغرق دينه (al-madyun al-mustaghraq daynuhu): A debtor whose debt covers all his wealth.

The validity of a transaction with ghabn depends on the agent's role, with three categories: only slight excused (guardians), both slight and gross excused (agents and partners), and neither excused (certain constrained agents).

Rulings for Agent in Purchase and Definition of Ghabn
Rulings for agent buying slaves and animals with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal consequences when an agent in purchase buys a defective or unsuitable slave or animal, and identify the Hanafi threshold for tolerable ghabn.

Core Idea
An agent must follow instructions; deviation shifts liability, and ghabn is defined by expert evaluation.

This lesson from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the rulings for an agent who buys slaves or animals that may be unsuitable or defective, depending on the principal's stated purpose. It also provides the Hanafi technical definition of ghabn (unacceptable overcharge) with specific percentages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal's instruction
Determine if the principal specified a purpose (e.g., for intercourse, for riding, for zihar) or gave absolute authority. The ruling often hinges on the presence or absence of such instructions.
If the principal says 'buy a slave girl' without further specification, the agent has more discretion.
2
Analyze the agent's deviation
Did the agent buy an item that does not match the instruction (e.g., black vs white, blind vs seeing)? If yes, the purchase may not bind the principal.
Deviation includes buying a different color, type, or with an incompatible defect.
3
Determine liability
If the agent deviated, check whether the purchase binds the principal or the agent. The text distinguishes cases where the agent knew or did not know, and whether the principal's purpose was stated.
For example, buying a blind slave for zihar binds the agent; buying the same without knowledge binds the principal but with a right of return.
4
Evaluate the item's suitability
Consider if the item is legally suitable for the stated purpose. For instance, 'raqaba' implies a complete slave fit for expiation; a blind slave does not qualify. Similarly, a mare may not qualify if the principal wanted a riding animal (though the text says a mare binds? Actually, it says buying a mare does not bind for riding).
The text states: 'ashara dabbatan li yarkabaha fashtara muhran... la yalzim al-amir' so a mare does not satisfy the condition.
5
Define ghabn
Understand the thresholds for tolerable ghabn: half a tenth for goods, a tenth for animals, a fifth for real estate. These define what is considered a gross overcharge that can invalidate a sale or affect liability.
Gross ghabn (fahish) is what falls outside the evaluation of arbitrators.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قال اشتر جارية أعتقها عن ظهاري لزم المأمور ولو لم يعلم به لزم الأمر وله الرد. ولو قال جاريتين لأطأهما فاشترى أختين أو جارية مع خالتها أو عمتها رضاعاً أو نسباً فخالف عند الثاني خلافاً لزفر وإن في صفقتين لا يكون مخالفاً . في القولين. ولو اشترى أمة وبنتها لا يكون مخالفاً لأن وطأها حلال له وإنما يحرم وطء إحداهما بوطئه الأخرى؛ ذكره في ا هـ. وفيها: وكله بشراء رقبة لم تجز العمياء لما علم أن الرقبة اسم للكاملة ا هـ . المنتقي فيفرق بين لفط رقبة وجارية فيتقيد الأوّل بما يجوز عتقه عن الكفارة دون الثاني، وفسر المؤلف ما يتغابن الناس فيه بما يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين فعلم منه أن الغبن الفاحش ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين وهذا هو الأصح كما في المعراج وفي السراج الوهاج معزياً إلى الخجندي: الذي يتغابن الناس في مثله نصف العشر أو أقل منه، فإن كان أكثر من العشر فهو مما لا يتغابن الناس فيه . وقال نصير بن يحيى : ما يتغابن الناس فيه في العروض نصف العشر، وفي الحيوان العشر، وفي العقار الخمس وما خرج عنه فهو مما لا يتغابن نصف بيع رب المال مال المضاربة) أي قبل ظهور الربح كما في جامع الفصولين أيضاً قوله: (وقال نصير بن يحيى الخ) قال الرملي : ما قاله نصير بن يحيى تفسير لما في بعض الكتب، وأما ما لا يتغابن فيه قيل في العروض دنيم وفي الحيوان ده بازده وفي العقار ده دوازده .
He said: (The mudarib and agent for buying a specific thing) is absolute in the disposal of the mudarib, and earlier from al-Munya it was mentioned that his sale with gross ghabn is permissible, but his purchase with it is against him; there is inconsistency unless it is interpreted as purchase. He said: (And in) from her dower equivalent, it is permissible due to lack of suspicion, and it is restricted to value because the agent for purchase is not restricted to cash; he may buy on credit, and the deferment is a right of both agent and principal. Unlike deferment after purchase with cash, which is for the agent alone, not the principal, as in al-Bazzaziyya. The principal is only bound by what he restricted. If he appointed him to buy a slave girl and he bought his foster sister: if he said 'a slave girl to have intercourse with', then it is on the agent; if he said absolutely, then it is on the principal. If a slave girl sworn to be freed is owned by the principal, or his mother or sister, it is binding on the principal. If he said 'to have intercourse with' or 'to employ', it binds the agent. If he said 'buy me a slave girl to have intercourse with' and he bought the sister of his mother or his wife or a woman in 'idda of another, it is permissible, and so is any woman halal in some case. It is said it is not permissible, and that is adopted. If he bought a minor who cannot be had intercourse with, or a Zoroastrian, Jew, or Christian, it binds the principal. A Sabian binds according to him contrary to them (Sahibayn). If he bought his sister-in-law or aunt by lineage or fosterage, he is disobedient. If he bought a slave girl who has a husband or is in 'idda from a irrevocable or revocable divorce, it binds the agent. If he appointed him to buy an animal to ride, and he bought a mare, or a blind one, or one with a severed hand, it does not bind the principal; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. It binds? In it: If he appointed him to buy a black one and he bought a white one, it is not valid. If he appointed him to buy a blind one and he bought a seeing one, it is valid. Similarly in agency for marriage. If he bought a stone-deaf woman without knowing, it is valid on the principal and he has the right of return. If he knew, then he is disobedient. Similarly if he did not know and the seller declared immunity from all defects. If he bought a blind slave girl and he said 'buy a slave girl to free for zihar', it binds the agent; if he did not know, it binds the principal and he has the right of return. If he said 'two slave girls to have intercourse with' and he bought two sisters or a slave girl with her maternal aunt or paternal aunt by fosterage or lineage, he is disobedient according to the second (Abu Yusuf or Muhammad?) contrary to Zufar. If in two transactions, he is not disobedient. In the two views. If he bought a female slave and her daughter, he is not disobedient because intercourse with her is halal for him; it only becomes haram upon intercourse with one. It is mentioned in... In it: If he appointed him to buy a slave (raqaba), a blind one is not valid because raqaba is the name for a complete one. Al-Muntaqa distinguishes between the word raqaba and jariya; the first is restricted to what is valid for emancipation in expiation, the second not. The author explained that what people tolerate ghabn in is what falls under the evaluation of arbitrators; thus, gross ghabn is what does not fall under their evaluation. This is the correct view as in al-Mi'raj and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj citing al-Khujandi: what people tolerate is half a tenth or less; if more than a tenth, it is not tolerated. Nasir ibn Yahya said: what is tolerated in goods is half a tenth, in animals a tenth, in real estate a fifth; beyond that is not tolerated. (Sale of capital owner of mudaraba funds) i.e., before profit appears, as in Jami' al-Fusulayn. Also he said: (And Nasir ibn Yahya's statement) al-Ramli said: what Nasir ibn Yahya said is an interpretation of what is in some books. As for what is not tolerated: it is said in goods one tenth (?), in animals ten to eleven (?), in real estate ten to twelve (?) (Persian numbers).

Commentary
This section provides detailed case rulings for an agent in purchase, particularly of slaves, animals, and items with specific conditions. It begins by clarifying that the mudarib and agent for a specific item have different rules for sale and purchase: sale with gross ghabn is allowed but purchase with gross ghabn is on the agent. Then it discusses various scenarios: buying a foster sister, buying for specific purposes (intercourse, freeing for zihar), buying defective items, buying a raqaba (which must be a complete slave valid for expiation). The passage also includes an important clarification from the author (صاحب الكنز) on the definition of ghabn: it is what falls under the evaluation of arbitrators. It then gives specific numerical definitions from Nasir ibn Yahya and al-Ramli for goods, animals, and real estate. This reinforces the earlier discussion on ghabn. The teacher should highlight the precision required in agency instructions and the consequences of deviation.

Key Terms
رقبة (raqaba): A complete slave (not blind) that can be used for emancipation in expiation.
غبن نصف العشر (ghabn nisf al-'ushr): Half a tenth (5%) as the threshold for tolerable ghabn in goods according to Nasir ibn Yahya.

Definition of Gross Fraud (Ghabn Fahish) and Its Thresholds
Defining ghabn fahish and its thresholds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of gross fraud (ghabn fahish) and distinguish between acceptable disparity and gross fraud using both the general definition (outside appraiser estimates) and the specific threshold guidelines.

Core Idea
Gross fraud is not a fixed percentage but any disparity outside expert appraiser estimates; thresholds like half-tenth are interpretive guidelines.

In sales, a price disparity that is too large can invalidate the transaction or give the defrauded party a right to rescind. Hanafi jurists define the threshold for such 'gross fraud' (ghabn fahish) first by reference to customary acceptance and expert appraisal. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the relied-upon definition and presents two scholarly attempts to set numeric guidelines for different asset types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Definition
The author states that acceptable disparity (ما يتغابن الناس فيه) is what falls within the range of expert appraisers. Therefore, gross fraud is what falls outside that range. This is the foundational definition.
The term 'al-ashahh' (the most correct) indicates this is the relied-upon position.
2
Distinguish Between Acceptable and Gross Disparity
Understand that 'taghabun' means mutual deception. People accept small disparities (they 'deceive each other' lightly), but gross fraud is too obvious to be overlooked.
The lexicographical root from al-Qamus confirms 'ghabn' means deception.
3
Examine the Two Scholarly Approaches to Thresholds
Al-Khujandi set a single threshold: up to half a tenth (5%) is acceptable; more than a tenth (10%) is gross fraud. Nasir ibn Yahya distinguished by asset type: half a tenth for movables, a tenth for animals, a fifth for real estate.
These are interpretive guidelines, not absolute rules.
4
Understand the Rationale Behind Different Thresholds
Nasir ibn Yahya explains that the more frequently a type of asset is traded, the smaller the acceptable disparity, because frequent transactions reduce the likelihood of fraud. Movables trade often, so half a tenth; real estate rarely, so a fifth.
This rationale ties the threshold to customary practice.
5
Apply the Definition to a Scenario
Given a sale where the market price is 100 and the buyer paid 130, ask: is the extra 30% within appraiser range? If appraisers say the usual margin is 10-15%, then 30% is gross fraud. If appraisers say a 30% margin is common for that item, then it is acceptable.
The definition remains flexible and custom-based.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفسر المؤلف ما يتغابن الناس فيه بما يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين فعلم منه أن الغبن الفاحش ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين وهذا هو الأصح كما في المعراج وفي السراج الوهاج معزياً إلى الخجندي: الذي يتغابن الناس في مثله نصف العشر أو أقل منه، فإن كان أكثر من العشر فهو مما لا يتغابن الناس فيه . وقال نصير بن يحيى : ما يتغابن الناس فيه في العروض نصف العشر، وفي الحيوان العشر، وفي العقار الخمس وما خرج عنه فهو مما لا يتغابن الناس فيه، ووجهه أن التصرف يكثر وجوده في العروض ويقل في العقار ويتوسط في الحيوان وكثرة الغبن لقلة التصرف ا هـ . والمراد بالتغابن الخداع فقولهم لا يتغابن الناس فيه معناه لا يخدع بعضهم بعضاً لفحشه وظهوره، وقولهم يتغابن الناس فيه أي يخدع بعضهم بعضاً لقلته. قال في القاموس : غبنه في البيع يغبنه غبناً ويحرك خدعه والتغابن أن يغبن بعضهم بعضاً ا هـ . وعلى هذا فقولهم غبن فاحش أي خداع قوله : (وقال نصير بن يحيى الخ) قال الرملي : ما قاله نصير بن يحيى تفسير لما في بعض الكتب، وأما ما لا يتغابن فيه قيل في العروض دنيم وفي الحيوان ده بازده وفي العقار ده دوازده .
And the author interpreted 'what people overlook in trading' as what falls within the valuation of appraisers. From this it is understood that gross fraud is what does not fall within the valuation of appraisers, and this is the most correct, as in al-Mi'raj and in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, attributed to al-Khujandi: 'What people overlook in its like is half a tenth or less. If it is more than a tenth, then it is something people do not overlook.' And Nasir ibn Yahya said: 'What people overlook in trading in movable goods is half a tenth; in animals, a tenth; in real estate, a fifth. Whatever exceeds this is what people do not overlook.' The reason is that transactions occur frequently in movable goods, rarely in real estate, and moderately in animals, and the frequency of fraud is due to lack of transactions. The meaning of taghabun is deception. So their statement 'people do not overlook it' means they do not deceive each other because of its excessiveness and obviousness. And their statement 'people overlook it' means they deceive each other because of its scarcity. He said in al-Qamus: 'He cheated him in the sale, he cheats him with cheating, and taghabun is when they cheat each other.' Based on this, their statement 'gross fraud' means deception. The author's saying: 'And Nasir ibn Yahya said...' al-Ramli said: 'What Nasir ibn Yahya said is an explanation found in some books. As for what is not overlooked, it is said: in movable goods, one-fortieth; in animals, one-tenth; in real estate, one-twelfth.'
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage defines the legal concept of 'gross fraud' (ghabn fahish). The author of Kanz al-Daqaiq defined it as a price disparity outside the range of expert appraisers. The commentator expands by presenting two scholarly opinions on specific thresholds: al-Khujandi says the acceptable disparity is up to half a tenth (5%) of the price; more than a tenth (10%) is gross fraud. Nasir ibn Yahya adds distinctions based on asset type: half a tenth for movable goods, a tenth for animals, and a fifth (20%) for real estate. The reasoning ties fraud frequency to transaction frequency. The lexicological root from al-Qamus confirms 'ghabn' means deception. The passage concludes with al-Ramli's note that Nasir's figures are interpretational, providing alternative ratios from some sources (one-fortieth for goods, tenth for animals, twelfth for land). The overall lesson: gross fraud is not strictly numerical but determined by custom and appraiser standards, though the stated figures serve as guidelines.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghabn al-fāḥish): A price disparity that exceeds what people ordinarily accept in trade, determined by custom and appraiser evaluation.
التغابن (al-taghābun): Mutual deception in a transaction where both parties overlook a minor disparity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When it exceeds half a tenth (5%) of the price.
B) When it exceeds one tenth (10%) of the price.
C) When it does not fall within the range of expert appraisers' valuations.
D) When it is more than one-fifth (20%) for real estate.

Key Takeaway
Gross fraud in the Hanafi school is defined by what falls outside expert appraiser estimates, not by a fixed percentage; specific thresholds like half-tenth or fifth are interpretive and vary by custom and asset type.

Selling or Buying Half a Slave: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Dispute on validity of agent selling or buying half a slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an agent selling half a slave, apply the concept of wasila, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Selling half a slave by an agent is valid only if the other half is sold before dispute, per the preferred view of the Sahibayn.

When an agent is authorized to sell a whole slave but sells only half, do we deem it valid? Abu Hanifa says yes because the command is absolute, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue it is a mere means (wasila) that must be completed to avoid the harm of forced partnership. The later preferred view adopts the Sahibayn's conditional validity, based on istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The issue is when an agent sells half a slave while authorized to sell the whole. State Abu Hanifa's view (valid absolutely) and the Sahibayn's view (valid only if the other half is sold before dispute).
The Sahibayn are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Analyze the evidence for each position
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas jali: selling the whole for half price is valid, so selling half is a fortiori valid. The Sahibayn use istihsan based on custom and the harm of partnership, treating the half sale as a wasila.
Wasila is a means that becomes valid only if the end is achieved.
3
Understand the concept of wasila and its role
The Sahibayn argue that selling half is only a means to fulfil the command. If the agent sells the remaining half before any dispute, the means is completed and the sale becomes valid. If not, it is invalid due to harm.
The same reasoning applies to buying half a slave, but with a difference explained later.
4
Recognize the mufta bihi and its practical effect
The text states that the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view, as per al-Hidayah. Practically, the sale is suspended until the other half is sold; otherwise, it is void.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa despite Abu Hanifa's contrary view.
5
Distinguish sale vs. purchase and additional cases
For purchase, buying half is suspended by agreement; if the other half is bought before the principal rejects, it is binding. For sale, Abu Hanifa's absolute view differs from the Sahibayn's conditional one provided the thing is divisible without harm.
The text also covers selling one of two slaves and selling for less than a fair share.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو وكل ببيع عبد فباع نصفه (صح) أي عند أبي حنيفة لأن اللفظ مطلق عن قيد الافتراق والاجتماع ألا ترى أنه لو باع الكل بثمن النصف يجوز عنده فإذا باع النصف أولى. وقالا : لا يجوز لأنه غير متعارف لما فيه من ضرر الشركة إلا أن يبيع النصف الآخر قبل أن يختصما لأن بيع النصف قد يقع وسيلة إلى الامتثال بأن لا يجد من يشتريه جملة فيحتاج إلى أن يفرق وإذا باع الباقي قبل نقض البيع الأول تبين أنه وقع وسيلة، وإذا لم يبع ظهر أنه لم يقع وسيلة فلا يجوز، وهذا استحسان عندهما؛ كذا في الهداية وهو يفيد ترجيح قولهما ولذا أخره مع دليله كما هو عادته، ولذا استشهد لقول الإمام بما لو باع الكل بثمن النصف فإنه يجوز ، وقد علمت أن المفتى به خلاف قوله. وفي الخزانة : أمر ببيع عبده بألف فباع نصفه بألف جاز بيعه بألف وقد أحسن وإن باع نصفه بألف إلا درهماً وكر حنطة بطل ا هـ . والمراد من العبد ما في تبعيضه ضرر احترازاً عما لا ضرر في تبعيضه كالحنطة والشعير فيجوز بيع البعض اتفاقاً؛ كذا في المعراج . وفي البزازية وكله ببيع عبدين فباع أحدهما جاز إن لم يكن فيه ضرر، وإن أحدهما أجود فعلى الخلاف. وكله ببيعهما بألف فباع أحدهما بأربعمائة إن كان ذلك حصة من الثمن أو أكثر جاز، وإن أقل فلا عند الأمام. وقالا : إن قدر ما يتغابن جاز ا هـ قوله : (وفي الشراء يتوقف ما لم يشتر الباقي يعني لو وكله بشراء عبد فاشترى نصفه فالشراء موقوف اتفاقاً فإن اشترى باقيه لزم الموكل لأن شراء البعض قد يقع وسيلة إلى الامتثال بأن كان موروثاً بين جماعة فيحتاج إلى شرائه شقصاً شقصاً، فإذا اشترى الباقي قبل رد الآمر البيع تبين أنه وسيلة فينفذ على الأمر وهذا بالاتفاق، والفرق لأبي حنيفة أن في الشراء تتحقق التهمة على ما مر وآخر أن الأمر بالبيع يصادف ملكه فيصح فيعتبر فيه إطلاقه والآمر بالشراء صادف ملك الغير فلم فلا يعتبر فيه التقييد والإطلاق.
His statement: (And if he authorized him to sell a slave and he sold half of it, it is valid) i.e., according to Abu Hanifa, because the wording is unrestricted by a condition of separation or union. Do you not see that if he sold the whole for the price of half, it is valid according to him, so selling half is even more appropriate? And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not valid because it is not customary, due to the harm of partnership, unless he sells the other half before they dispute. Because selling half may occur as a means to compliance, if he cannot find a buyer for the whole and needs to split it. If he sells the remainder before the first sale is rescinded, it becomes clear that it was a means; if he does not sell it, it becomes clear that it was not a means, so it is not valid. This is istihsan according to them. Thus it is in al-Hidayah, and it indicates a preference for their statement, so he (the author) delayed it with its evidence as is his habit. Therefore, he cited the Imam's statement about selling the whole for half the price being valid as evidence. And you have learned that the mufta bihi is contrary to his statement. In al-Khazanah: If he ordered to sell his slave for 1000 and he sold half of it for 1000, his sale is valid for 1000 and he did well; but if he sold half for 1000 minus one dirham and a load of wheat, it is void. The intent of 'slave' is that which has harm in dividing it, as opposed to things that have no harm in division, like wheat and barley, so selling part is unanimously valid. Thus in al-Mi'raj. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: If he authorized him to sell two slaves and he sold one of them, it is valid if there is no harm; if one is superior, then the dispute applies. If he authorized him to sell both for 1000 and he sold one for 400, if that is the share of the price or more, it is valid; if less, then according to the Imam it is not valid. The two said: if it is within the amount that people overlook, it is valid. His statement: (And in purchase, it is suspended until he buys the remainder) meaning if he authorized him to buy a slave and he bought half of it, the purchase is suspended by agreement. If he buys the remainder, it is binding on the principal, because buying part may occur as a means to compliance, such as when the slave is inherited among a group and he needs to buy shares piecemeal. So if he buys the remainder before the principal rejects the sale, it is clear it was a means and it takes effect on the principal by agreement. The difference according to Abu Hanifa is that in purchase, suspicion (tuhma) is verified, and that the command to sell encounters his ownership so it is valid, so its absolute nature is considered; while the command to purchase encounters the property of another, so it is not valid, and thus restriction and absolute nature are not considered.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether an agent can validly sell or buy only half of a slave when authorized to sell or buy a whole. Abu Hanifa holds that selling half is valid because the command is absolute and selling half is a fortiori valid since selling the whole for half price is valid. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, arguing that the sale is not valid unless the other half is sold before the parties dispute; it is a means (wasila) to fulfilling the command, and if not completed it causes unjustified partnership. Their view is based on istihsan (juristic preference) due to the harm of partnership and custom. The text notes that the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is the Sahibayn's view, as indicated in al-Hidayah. The passage then provides additional cases: if the agent sells one of two slaves, it depends on harm; if the agent sells one for less than its share, Abu Hanifa invalidates it, while the Sahibayn allow if within acceptable disparity. For purchase, there is consensus that buying half is suspended; if the other half is bought before the principal rejects it becomes binding. The distinction between sale and purchase is based on ownership: sale involves the principal's property, so absolute command suffices; purchase involves a third party's property, so tuhma (suspicion of collusion) necessitates suspension.

Key Terms
وسيلة (wasīlah): A means or intermediate act that leads to fulfilling the principal's command, such as selling half to eventually sell the whole.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a stronger reason (custom, necessity, or avoidance of hardship).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in this text, when is an agent's sale of half a slave valid?
A) Whenever the agent acts in the principal's interest.
B) Only if the other half is sold before the parties dispute.
C) Always valid, because the command is absolute.
D) Only if the price equals half the market value.

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi position is that an agent's sale of half a slave is a conditional wasila: valid only if the other half is sold before dispute, based on istihsan to avoid harm of partnership.
