Proving Agency for Sale Before a Judge
Ways for an agent to prove his authority to sell property in court

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three methods by which an agent can prove his agency for sale before a judge and explain the role of evidence in each.

Core Idea
An agent must prove agency in court to prevent the principal's later denial.

When an agent is appointed to sell a specific asset, he may need to prove that authority in court to protect the sale from future challenges. Khizanat al-Muftin provides three practical stratagems for this. Each method involves presenting evidence (bayyinah) before a judge to secure a binding ruling. Understanding these methods is essential for anyone involved in sales through an agent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Why would an agent need to prove agency? Because the principal might later deny the appointment, making the sale invalid or causing liability for the buyer.
The agent seeks a judicial declaration to bind the principal and third parties.
2
List the three methods
Summarize each method from the text: (1) Handing the asset to a third party and proving agency against them. (2) Selling directly but having the buyer refuse possession, then proving agency to compel delivery. (3) The buyer suing the agent, who denies agency, and the buyer proving agency against the agent.
All methods ultimately rely on presenting evidence (bayyinah).
3
Determine the common requirement
What is required in every method? The agent (or the buyer) must present evidence (bainah) to the judge that the agent is authorized by the principal.
The evidence must be such that the judge can rule on the agency.
4
Analyse the legal effect
Once the agency is proven, the judge orders the relevant party (possessor or buyer) to cooperate, and the agent can proceed with the sale or delivery. The principal's later denial is not heeded.
The judicial ruling is binding and protects the transaction.
5
Note the practical impact
These stratagems allow agents to conduct sales smoothly and give buyers confidence, reducing the risk of later disputes.
They are examples of Hanafi procedural fiqh facilitating commerce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي خزانة المفتين : رجل وكل رجلاً ببيع عين من أعيان ماله فأراد الوكيل أن يثبت الوكالة بالبيع عند القاضي حتى لو جاء الموكل وأنكر لا يلتفت إلى إنكاره فله وجوه أحدها أن يسلم الوكيل العين إلى رجل ثم يدعي أنه وكيل من مالكه بالقبض والبيع فسلمه لي فيقول ذو اليد لا علم لي بالوكالة فيقيم البيئة على أنه وكيله بالقبض والبيع فيسمع القاضي ذلك ويأمره بالتسليم إليه فيبيعه. وثانيها أن يقول هذا ملك فلان أبيعه منك فإذا باعه منه يأمره بقبض المبيع فيقول المشتري لا أقبض منك لأني أخاف أن يجيء المالك وينكر الوكالة وربما يكون المقبوض في يدي أو يحصل منه نقصان فيضمنني فيقيم الوكيل بينة أنه وكيل فلان بالبيع والتسليم ويجبره على القبض ويثبت بإقامة البيئة ولاية الجبر على القبض. وثالثها رجل ادعى أن الدار التي في يدك ملك فلان وأنت وكيله بالبيع وقد بعت فقال بعت منك ولكن لست بوكيل من فلان ولم يوكلني بالبيع فأقام مدعي الشراء البينة على أنه وكيل فلان بالبيع فهو خصم حتى تقبل البينة عليه ويثبت كونه وكيلاً عنه في البيع.
And in Khizanat al-Muftin: A man appointed another man to sell a specific asset from his property. The agent wanted to prove the agency for sale before the judge so that even if the principal comes and denies, his denial is not heeded. So he has several ways: First, that the agent hands over the asset to a man, then claims that he is the agent of its owner for taking possession and sale, so he handed it to me. Then the possessor says, 'I have no knowledge of the agency.' So he presents evidence that he is his agent for taking possession and sale, and the judge hears that and orders him to hand it over to him, and he sells it. Second, that he says, 'This is the property of so-and-so; I sell it to you.' When he sells it to him, he orders him to take possession of the sold item. The buyer says, 'I will not take possession from you because I fear that the owner may come and deny the agency, and perhaps the property is in my hand or damage may occur, and then he will hold me liable.' So the agent presents evidence that he is the agent of so-and-so for sale and delivery, and he compels him to take possession, and by presenting evidence, the authority to compel possession is established. Third, a man claims, 'The house in your hand is the property of so-and-so, and you are his agent for sale, and I have bought it.' The agent says, 'I sold it to you, but I am not an agent of so-and-so, and he did not appoint me for sale.' So the claimant of purchase presents evidence that he is the agent of so-and-so for sale. Then he is an opponent so that evidence is accepted against him, and it is established that he is an agent for sale.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage from Khizanat al-Muftin presents three legal stratagems for an agent appointed to sell a specific item to judicially establish the agency. The purpose is to prevent the principal from later denying the agency, which would jeopardize the sale. The first method: the agent transfers the item to a third party (making that party the possessor), then claims agency to take possession and sell. The possessor denies knowledge, and the agent proves the agency in court. The judge then orders the possessor to hand over the item to the agent, who can then sell it. The second method: the agent directly sells to a buyer but the buyer refuses to take possession, fearing the principal's denial. The agent proves the agency in court, and the judge compels the buyer to take possession. The third method: a person claims to have bought the house from the agent, but the agent denies being an agent. The buyer then proves the agency against the agent (now considered an opponent), and the agency is established. These stratagems rely on presenting evidence (bayyinah) before a judge to secure a ruling that binds both the principal and third parties. The text illustrates practical ways an agent can use the court system to protect the validity of his actions.

Key Terms
وكيل بالبيع (wakīl bil-bay‘): An agent appointed to sell a specific asset on behalf of the principal.
جبر على القبض (jabr ‘alā al-qabd): Compulsion of the buyer to take possession of the purchased item when the seller's authority is confirmed.
بيّنة (bayyinah): Evidence presented in court, often witness testimony or documentary proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To avoid liability for the asset
B) To create a conflict that forces the agent to present evidence
C) Because he truly does not know
D) To protect the principal's rights

Key Takeaway
An agent can preemptively prove agency in court using one of three methods, all requiring evidence to bind the principal and third parties.

Limits of the Agent for Receipt: Pledging and Compensation
Rulings on agent's authority and compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that an agent for receipt cannot pledge the property and explain the validity of wage for receipt versus debt collection.

Core Idea
An agent for receipt cannot pledge; wage for deposit receipt is valid but for debt collection requires time specification.

In this lesson, we examine two rulings from Bahr al-Raiq that define the boundaries of an agent's authority in receipt (wakalah bil qabd). The first ruling prohibits the agent from pledging the property received, with consequences if he does. The second ruling addresses compensation: an agent may be paid for receiving a deposit, but for collecting a debt, a wage is only valid if a time is specified. These rules illustrate the Hanafi principle that agency is restricted to the specific mandate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the agent prohibited from doing? (pledging). What is the consequence if he does? (suspension, depositor liable).
Focus on the phrase 'بقبض العين لا'.
2
Understand the consequence
The depositor becomes liable and can recourse against the agent. Trace the chain: agent pledges -> principal sells -> matter stops -> depositor pays -> recovers from agent.
The liability moves from the principal to the depositor.
3
Analyze the wage rulings
There are two separate cases: wage for receiving a deposit (valid) and wage for collecting a debt (invalid unless time is specified). Distinguish the nature of the actions.
Receiving a deposit is a single act; debt collection is ongoing and may involve risk.
4
Apply the principle
No istihsan here; the rulings are based on the scope of authority and the need to avoid uncertainty (gharar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة باب الوكالة بالخصومة والقبض وبقبض العين لا فلو برهن ذو اليد على الوكيل بالقبض إن الموكل باعه وقف الأمر ضمن المودع رجع على الوكيل وإذا وكله بقبضها اليوم فله قبضها غداً استحساناً، ولو قال اقبضها بمحضر فلان فقبضها في غيبته جاز، ولو أنكر ربها التوكيل وحلف وضمن المودع فله الرجوع على القابض إن كانت قائمة فإن ادعى الوكيل هلاكها أو الدفع إلى الموكل وقد صدقه المودع في الوكالة لم يرجع عليه، وإن كان كذبه أو لم يصدقه ولم يكذبه أو صدقه وضمنه المال كان له أن يضمنه ولو جعل للوكيل بقبض الوديعة أجراً جاز وعلى تقاضي الدين لا إلا أن يوقت ا هـ .
The Book of Agency, Chapter on Agency for Litigation and Receipt. And regarding receipt of the physical item: no. So if the person in possession presents proof that the agent for receipt (that the principal sold it) the matter stops, the depositor is liable and has recourse against the agent. If he authorized him to receive it today, he may receive it tomorrow by istihsan. If he said 'Receive it in the presence of so-and-so', and he received it in his absence, it is valid. If the owner denies the authorization and swears, and the depositor is liable, he may have recourse against the receiver if it is still in existence. If the agent claims it was destroyed or that he paid it to the principal, and the depositor affirms the agency, he has no recourse. But if he denies it, or neither affirms nor denies, or affirms and is made liable for the property, he may hold him liable. If he sets a wage for the agent for receiving the deposit, it is valid; but for collecting a debt, it is not valid unless he specifies a time. End.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the agent appointed for receipt (qabd). The author begins by stating that an agent for receipt of a physical item (al-ayn) does not have the right to give a pledge on it. He then discusses various scenarios: if the agent gives a pledge and the principal sells, the matter is suspended; if the depositor is made liable, he can recover from the agent. By istihsan (juristic preference), an agent authorized to receive today may receive tomorrow. If the principal says 'receive in the presence of so-and-so', the agent may validly receive even in that person's absence. If the owner of the property (the depositor) denies the agency and swears an oath, and the depository is made liable, the depository can recover from the receiver if the property still exists. But if the agent claims destruction or payment to the principal, and the depository confirms the agency, no recourse is available. Various outcomes depend on the depository's stance. The agent may be given a wage for receiving a deposit, but for collecting a debt, a wage is only valid if a time is specified.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakālah): Agency
قبض (qabḍ): Receipt, taking possession

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a wage for an agent collecting a debt is valid only if:
A) The agent is also a guarantor.
B) A time is specified.
C) The debt exceeds 10 dirhams.
D) The principal agrees verbally.

Key Takeaway
An agent for receipt cannot pledge the property, and compensation for debt collection requires time specification to be valid.

Temporal and Locational Flexibility in Receipt by Agent
Rulings on time and witness conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to allow receipt the next day and explain the validity of receipt without the designated witness.

Core Idea
By istihsan, an agent may receive the next day; a condition to receive in a presence is not strict.

This lesson explores two rulings that provide flexibility to the agent in carrying out his task. The first ruling, based on istihsan (juristic preference), allows an agent authorized to receive today to also receive tomorrow. The second ruling states that if a principal specifies a witness for the receipt, the agent's receipt in that witness's absence is still valid. These rulings reflect the Hanafi tendency to facilitate transactions and avoid strictness when the purpose is achievable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First scenario: authorization to receive 'today' (al-yawm). Second scenario: instruction to receive 'in the presence of so-and-so'.
Both involve conditions on the manner of receipt.
2
Apply istihsan to the time condition
Qiyas would restrict receipt to the specific day. Istihsan, based on custom and necessity, allows receipt the next day because the purpose is to take possession, not to adhere to a literal day.
The departure is from strict analogy to a more practical rule.
3
Analyze the witness condition
The phrase 'in the presence of so-and-so' is not a condition (shart) but a mere specification (ta'yin). The agent fulfills the mandate by receiving, even without the witness.
This distinguishes between a mandatory condition and a recommended or precautionary instruction.
4
Derive the underlying principle
In both cases, the agent's act of valid receipt (qabd) is the core; external conditions are interpreted liberally to achieve the objective.
This aligns with the maxim: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by their objectives).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة باب الوكالة بالخصومة والقبض وبقبض العين لا فلو برهن ذو اليد على الوكيل بالقبض إن الموكل باعه وقف الأمر ضمن المودع رجع على الوكيل وإذا وكله بقبضها اليوم فله قبضها غداً استحساناً، ولو قال اقبضها بمحضر فلان فقبضها في غيبته جاز، ولو أنكر ربها التوكيل وحلف وضمن المودع فله الرجوع على القابض إن كانت قائمة فإن ادعى الوكيل هلاكها أو الدفع إلى الموكل وقد صدقه المودع في الوكالة لم يرجع عليه، وإن كان كذبه أو لم يصدقه ولم يكذبه أو صدقه وضمنه المال كان له أن يضمنه ولو جعل للوكيل بقبض الوديعة أجراً جاز وعلى تقاضي الدين لا إلا أن يوقت ا هـ .
The Book of Agency, Chapter on Agency for Litigation and Receipt. And regarding receipt of the physical item: no. So if the person in possession presents proof that the agent for receipt (that the principal sold it) the matter stops, the depositor is liable and has recourse against the agent. If he authorized him to receive it today, he may receive it tomorrow by istihsan. If he said 'Receive it in the presence of so-and-so', and he received it in his absence, it is valid. If the owner denies the authorization and swears, and the depositor is liable, he may have recourse against the receiver if it is still in existence. If the agent claims it was destroyed or that he paid it to the principal, and the depositor affirms the agency, he has no recourse. But if he denies it, or neither affirms nor denies, or affirms and is made liable for the property, he may hold him liable. If he sets a wage for the agent for receiving the deposit, it is valid; but for collecting a debt, it is not valid unless he specifies a time. End.

Liability and Recourse Between Depositor and Agent
Rulings on liability and recourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when the depositor can seek recourse against the agent based on the agent's claims and the owner's confirmation of agency.

Core Idea
The depositor's right of recourse depends on the existence of the property and the acknowledgment of agency.

This lesson covers the complex scenarios of liability when the owner of the deposit denies the agency. The passage from Bahr al-Raiq details the circumstances under which the depositor (mudiʿ) can recover from the agent (qābiḍ) after having been made liable to the owner. The rulings turn on whether the agent claims the property was destroyed or paid to the principal, and whether the depositor affirms or denies the agency. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for legal practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario
The owner denies the agency and takes an oath; the depositor is then liable to the owner.
The depositor must pay the value of the property to the owner.
2
Determine recourse when property exists
If the property is still in existence (qā'imah) with the agent, the depositor can recover it from the agent.
Recourse: الرجوع على القابض إن كانت قائمة.
3
Analyze cases when property is claimed destroyed or paid
If the agent claims destruction or payment to the principal, the depositor's recourse depends on whether he affirms (ṣaddaqa) the agency.
Affirmation bars recourse; denial or uncertainty allows recourse.
4
Examine the depositor's options when he affirms and is liable
Even if the depositor affirms the agency, if he is made liable (ḍamina), he can still hold the agent liable.
This is a nuance: affirmation does not automatically preclude liability.

Source Text

Invalidity of Guarantor's Agency and Debtor's Self-Discharge
Critical refinement of the ruling on guarantor's agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a guarantor's agency being invalid, explain the qiyas to the slave case, and distinguish the debtor's authorization to discharge himself as a valid exception.

Core Idea
A guarantor cannot be the creditor's agent because he works for himself; a debtor can authorize another to discharge him because he also works for the creditor.

This lesson explores a key ruling in Hanafi fiqh: the invalidity of a guarantor (kafil) acting as the creditor's agent. Why is this invalid? Because an agent must work solely for the principal, but the guarantor would be discharging his own debt, thus acting for himself. An analogy to an emancipated slave clarifies the reasoning. An important objection arises: what about a debtor authorizing someone to discharge himself? That is valid—an exception that illuminates the underlying condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its foundation
State the ruling from the matn: 'the agency of the guarantor for the money is invalid.' Understand the reasoning: the agent must work for another, but a valid agency would make him work for himself by discharging his own liability. Thus the essential condition (rukn) is absent.
The core principle: al-wakil ya'malu li ghayrihi (the agent works for another).
2
Analyze the qiyas (analogy) to the slave case
Consider the case of an indebted slave emancipated by his master, with the master guaranteeing the slave's value to creditors. If the creditor appoints that slave as his agent to collect from the slave himself, it would be invalid for the same reason: the slave would be working for himself. This analogy from al-Hidayah illustrates the illa (effective cause): the agent acts for himself.
The qiyas is jaliy (clear analogy) with an explicit illa.
3
Address the objection: debtor authorizing self-discharge
An objection is raised: a debtor can validly authorize another to discharge him (e.g., 'I appoint you to drop my debt'), even though that agent acts for himself by freeing the debtor's liability. Why is this valid? Because the agent also acts for the creditor by dropping the debt.
The condition is that the agent acts for another, not that he does not act for himself. Here the agent serves both parties.
4
Refute the alternative view that it is tamlik, not tawkeel
A commentator argued that the debtor's authorization is actually tamlik (transfer of ownership) like saying to one's wife 'Divorce yourself!'—not agency. The author refutes this: if it were tamlik, the creditor could not revoke it before the discharge, but he can revoke. Hence it remains tawkeel.
This demonstrates applying usul al-fiqh to distinguish between legal categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبطل توكيل الكفيل بالمال لأن الوكيل من يعمل لغيره ولو صححناها صار عاملاً لنفسه في إبراء ذمته فانعدم الركن لأن قبول قوله ملازم للوكالة لكونه أميناً، ولو صححناها لا تقبل لكونه مبرئاً نفسه فيعدم بانعدام لازمه وهو نظير عبد مديون أعتقه مولاه حتى ضمن قيمته للغرماء ويطالب العبد بجميع الدين فلو وكله الطالب بقبض المال من العبد كان باطلاً لما بيناه ؛ كذا في الهداية. وأورد توكيل المديون بإبراء نفسه فإنه صحيح مع كونه عاملاً لنفسه والتحقيق في جوابه ما في منية المفتي من قوله : ولو وكله بإبراء نفسه لأنه وإن كان عاملاً لنفسه بتفريغ ذمته فهو عامل لرب الدين بإسقاط دينه، وشرط يصح الوكالة كونه عاملاً لغيره لا كونه غير عامل لنفسه ا هـ . وأما قول الشارح في جوابه إنه تمليك وليس بتوكيل كما في قوله لامرأته طلقي نفسك فسهو ظاهر إذ لو كان تمليكاً لم يصح رجوع الدائن عنه قبل إبراء نفسه مع أنه يصح . وفي تلخيص الجامع : لو قال الدائن لمديون
His statement: (And the agency of the guarantor for the money is invalid because the agent is one who works for another, and if we validate it, he would be working for himself in discharging his own liability, so the pillar (rukn) is absent because acceptance of his statement is concomitant with agency due to his being trustworthy. And if we validate it, it would not be accepted because he is discharging himself, so it becomes absent by the absence of its concomitant. This is analogous to a indebted slave whom his master emancipated such that he guarantees his value to the creditors, and the slave is demanded for the entire debt. If the claimant authorized him to receive the money from the slave, it would be invalid for the reason we stated. This is in al-Hidayah. And an objection was raised: the authorization of the debtor to discharge himself is valid even though he is acting for himself. The verification of its answer is in Munyat al-Mufti from his statement: 'If he authorized him to discharge himself, although he is acting for himself by freeing his liability, he is also acting for the creditor by dropping his debt, and the condition for validity of agency is that he is acting for another, not that he is not acting for himself.' End. As for the commentator's statement in his answer that it is tamlik (transfer of ownership) and not tawkeel (agency), like his statement to his wife 'Divorce yourself,' it is an obvious oversight, because if it were tamlik, it would not be valid for the creditor to revoke it before he discharges himself, whereas it is valid. And in Talkhis al-Jami': if the creditor says to the debtor...
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the ruling on the invalidity of a guarantor's agency. The author, al-Haskafi, is commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq which states that the agency of a guarantor (kafil) for the money is invalid. The rationale is that an agent must work for another, but if this agency were valid, the guarantor would be working for himself by discharging his own liability, thus the essential condition is absent. An analogy is given of a slave who is emancipated but owes debt: the creditor cannot validly appoint that slave as an agent to collect from himself. The objection is raised: what about the debtor who authorizes someone to discharge himself? That is valid even though the agent is acting for himself. The answer from Munyat al-Mufti clarifies that the agent, though acting for himself by freeing his liability, also acts for the creditor by dropping the debt; the condition is not that he does not act for himself, but that he acts for another as well. The commentator then refutes the claim that this is tamlik (transfer) rather than tawkeel, pointing out that if it were tamlik, the creditor could not revoke it, but he can revoke before the discharge occurs. The passage ends with an incomplete quote from Talkhis al-Jami'.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafīl): Guarantor; a person who stands surety for a debt, becoming liable for payment if the principal debtor defaults.
إبراء (ibrā'): Release or discharge; a legal act by which a creditor drops a debt owed to him, freeing the debtor from liability.
تمليك (tamlīk): Transfer of ownership; a legal act that vests title in another person, e.g., gift or sale.
وكيل (wakīl): Agent; a person appointed to act on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, why is the agency of a guarantor (kafil) invalid?
A) Because the guarantor is not trustworthy.
B) Because the principal did not consent.
C) Because the guarantor would be acting for himself by discharging his own liability.
D) Because the debtor already paid.

Key Takeaway
A guarantor cannot be the creditor's agent because he works for himself; but a debtor can authorize another to discharge him because that agent also works for the creditor.

Agent Returning Slave Girl: Seller Claims Buyer's Satisfaction
Sharh analyzing intra-Hanafi dispute on swearing the buyer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish Abu Hanifa's position from that of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding whether the buyer must be sworn when a seller claims satisfaction, and explain the underlying principle of 'māḍā ʿalā al-ṣiḥḥa'.

Core Idea
A court ruling valid on its face cannot be undone by later discovery of error according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a court ruling when error is later discovered. The case involves an agent returning a defective slave girl, with the seller claiming the buyer was already satisfied. The key question: can the buyer prevent the return by swearing? Abu Hanifa says no, because the ruling is externally valid; the two companions say yes, because the ruling was invalid. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of the school's epistemology of judicial rulings and the concept of tadāruk (rectification).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify Abu Hanifa's view: the slave girl is not returned to the seller, and the buyer is not sworn, because the court's ruling of rescission is considered valid on its face (māḍin ʿalā al-ṣiḥḥa) even if error appears later.
Abu Hanifa sees the ruling as final procedurally; swearing the buyer would serve no benefit.
2
Identify the opposing view (two companions)
State that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the slave girl should not be returned until the buyer is sworn, because they consider the ruling invalid (bāṭil) if error appears, so rectification is possible.
They view the ruling as open to correction.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The two companions argue by analogy: just as in the debt case rectification is possible by returning what the agent took, here too the return can be delayed until the buyer is sworn.
Their proof is based on the possibility of tadāruk.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The sharh notes that for Abu Hanifa, the difference is that in the slave girl case the ruling is māḍin ʿalā al-ṣiḥḥa, so rectification is impossible. The text adds that Abu Yusuf's most correct view is to delay in both cases (debt and slave girl).
Abu Yusuf's refined position aligns with the two companions' general approach.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the return is final and immediate; under the two companions, the return is delayed until the buyer is sworn, allowing the buyer to confirm or deny satisfaction.
This affects the outcome of the transaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن وكله بعيب في أمة وادعى البائع رضا المشتري لم يرد عليه حتى يحلف المشتري) والفرق أن التدارك ممكن هنالك باسترداد ما قبضه الوكيل إذا ظهر الخطأ عند نكوله وفي الثانية غير ممكن لأن القضاء بالفسخ ماض على الصحة وإن ظهر الخطأ عند أبي حنيفة كما هو ،مذهبه ولا يستحلف المشتري عنده بعد ذلك لأنه لا يفيد، فأما عندهما فالواجب أن يتحد الجواب على هذا في الفصلين ولا يؤخر لأن التدارك ممكن عندهما لبطلان القضاء. وقيل: الأصح أبي يوسف أن يؤخر في الفصلين لأنه يعتبر النظر حتى يستحلف المشتري لو كان حاضراً من غير دعوى البائع، فلو ردها الوكيل على البائع بالعيب في مسألة الكتاب فحضر الموكل وصدق على الرضا كانت له لا للبائع عند الكل على الأصح لأن القضاء لم يكن عن دليل موجب للنقض وإنما كان لجهل بالدليل المسقط للرد وهو الرضا ثم ظهر الدليل بخلافه فلا ينفذ باطناً؛ كذا في النهاية .
His statement: (If he entrusted him with returning a slave girl due to a defect, and the seller claims the buyer was satisfied, it is not returned to him until the buyer is sworn.) And the difference is that rectification is possible there by taking back what the agent received if error becomes apparent upon his [the agent's] refusal [to take an oath], while in the second case it is not possible because the ruling of rescission is valid on its face even if error becomes apparent, according to Abu Hanifa as is his madhhab; and the buyer is not sworn thereafter in his view because it would not be beneficial. As for according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], the answer must be uniform in both cases and not delayed because rectification is possible in their view due to the invalidity of the ruling. And it is said: the most correct view of Abu Yusuf is to delay in both cases because he considers the benefit, so the buyer would be sworn if he were present without the seller's claim. If the agent returned her to the seller due to the defect in the issue of the book, then the principal came and confirmed the satisfaction, it belongs to him, not to the seller, according to all, on the most correct view, because the ruling was not based on evidence necessitating annulment; rather it was due to ignorance of the evidence that precludes return, which is satisfaction, then the evidence appeared contrary to it, so it does not take effect inwardly; thus in al-Nihayah.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement discussing an inter-madhhab dispute regarding an agent entrusted to return a defective slave girl. If the seller claims the buyer was satisfied (thus no return), the slave girl is not returned to the seller until the buyer is sworn. The sharh explains the difference between this case and a previous one: in the previous case (debt recovery), rectification is possible by returning what the agent took if error appears; here, rectification is not possible for Abu Hanifa because the court's ruling of rescission is considered valid externally, even if error is later discovered. Therefore, swearing the buyer is useless for Abu Hanifa. However, for Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the ruling is invalid if error appears, so rectification is possible, and thus they would swear the buyer to delay the return. The most correct view of Abu Yusuf is to delay in both cases. If the principal later confirms satisfaction, the slave girl goes to him, not the seller, because the original ruling was based on ignorance of the evidence.

Key Terms
التدارك (al-tadāruk): Rectification or correction of a legal situation after a ruling has been issued.
مضى على الصحة (maḍā 'alā al-ṣiḥḥa): A ruling that is considered valid and final on its face, even if internal error exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the buyer not sworn when the seller claims satisfaction in the case of a defective slave girl?
A) Because the buyer is not present
B) Because the court's ruling of rescission is valid on its face and cannot be undone
C) Because the agent's testimony is sufficient
D) Because the seller's claim is automatically accepted

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the possibility of rectifying a court ruling after error discovery depends on whether the ruling is considered valid on its face (Abu Hanifa) or invalid if error appears (the two companions).

Agent Spending Own Money on Family: Ruling of Exchange
Sharah explaining the ruling when an agent spends his own money instead of the principal's for family expenses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an agent spends his own money instead of the principal's and explain the basis of istihsan over qiyas.

Core Idea
When an agent spends his own money while the principal's money is available, it is an exchange, not a gift.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key Hanafi principle in agency law. When a principal gives money to an agent to spend on the family, and the agent uses his own funds instead, the Hanafi school rules that an exchange takes place. This lesson unpacks the distinction between qiyas (which would treat the agent as a volunteer) and istihsan (which validates the exchange), a hallmark of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an agent spending his own money to fulfill the principal's order. The ruling is that the agent's money is exchanged for the principal's money (sahih).
The text states 'فالعشرة بالعشرة'.
2
Locate the dalil
The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference). The text says the agent for spending is like an agent for purchase.
Istihsan overrides qiyas.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The connection: the agent's spending is analogous to a purchase; by using his own funds while the principal's are present, he in effect buys the principal's money. Thus the exchange is valid.
The illa is the agent's performance of the task with his own funds when the principal's are available.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some argue qiyas would make the agent a volunteer (mutabarri‘) with no right to reimbursement. The Hanafi response is that istihsan applies due to the analogy with purchase.
The ikhtilaf is between istihsan (relied upon) and qiyas (minority view).
5
Understand the condition
The ruling applies only if the principal's money was still existent at the time of spending. If consumed, the agent becomes a volunteer.
This condition is from al-Nihayah reference in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن دفع إلى رجل عشرة ينفقها على أهله فأنفق عليهم عشرة من عنده فالعشرة بالعشرة) لأن الوكيل بالإنفاق وكيل بالشراء وحكمه كذلك، وقيل هذا استحسان، والقياس ويصير متبرعاً، وقيل القياس والاستحسان في قضاء الدين لأنه ليس بشراء، فأما الإنفاق فيضمن الشراء فلا يدخلا منه وظاهر كلامه أنه أنفق دراهمه مع بقاء دراهم الموكل ولذا قال في النهاية : هذا إذا كانت عشرة الدافع قائمة وقت الإنفاق وكان يضيف العقد إليها أو يطلق، أما إذا كانت مستهلكة أو أضاف العقد إلى عشرة نفسه. مشترياً لنفسه والأهل ليس بقيد احترازي لأنه لا فرق بين هـ. يصير متبرعا بالإنفاق لأن الدراهم تتعين في الوكالة ا الوكيل بالإنفاق في البيت والوكيل بالإنفاق في البناء كما في الخلاصة. والوكيل بالإنفاق ليس احترازياً أيضاً لأن الوكيل بقضاء الدين كذلك. وفي الخلاصة: الوكيل ببيع الدينار إذا أمسك الدينار وباع ديناره لا يصح، والوكيل بالشراء إذا اشترى ما أمر به ثم أنفق الدراهم
His statement: (And if someone gave a man ten [dirhams] to spend on his family, and he spent ten from his own [money] on them, then the ten are in exchange for the ten.) Because the agent for spending is an agent for purchase, and its ruling is the same. And it is said: this is istihsan, and the qiyas would be that he becomes a volunteer (mutabarri‘). And it is said: qiyas and istihsan are in the repayment of debt because it is not a purchase. As for spending, it includes purchase, so it does not enter into it? And the apparent meaning of his speech is that he spent his own dirhams while the principal's dirhams remained. Hence in al-Nihayah: this is if the ten of the giver were existent at the time of spending, and he attributed the contract to them or was absolute. But if they were consumed or he attributed the contract to his own ten, buying for himself — and 'family' is not a restrictive qualification because there is no difference between spending on family and other spending? He becomes a volunteer in spending because the dirhams are specified in the agency? The agent for spending in the house and the agent for spending in construction, as in al-Khulasa. And the agent for spending is not restrictive either because the agent for repaying debt is likewise. And in al-Khulasa: The agent for selling a dinar, if he kept the dinar and sold his own dinar, it is not valid. And the agent for purchase, if he bought what he was ordered to then spent the dirhams ...
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe discussing the ruling when an agent given money to spend on the principal's family instead spends his own money. The Hanafi ruling is that if the agent spends his own money while the principal's money is still available, it is considered an exchange: the agent's ten dirhams are exchanged for the principal's ten, so the agent becomes entitled to the principal's money. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference), as the agent is considered an agent for purchase (the family expenses are purchases), and by spending his own, he effectively buys the principal's money. The qiyas would make him a volunteer (mutabarri‘) with no right to reimbursement. The text clarifies that this applies only if the principal's money is still existent at the time of spending; if it was consumed, the agent becomes a volunteer. The ruling applies to any agent authorized to spend, not just for family, as confirmed in al-Nihayah and al-Khulasa.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that allows a ruling contrary to qiyas for a reason of equity or custom.
متبرع (mutabarri‘): A person who acts voluntarily without expectation of compensation; the qiyas ruling would consider the agent as such if he spends his own money.
الوكيل بالإنفاق (al-wakīl bi al-infaq): Agent authorized to spend money on behalf of the principal (e.g., for family expenses).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The ten of the agent are exchanged for the ten of the principal
C) The agent must return the ten to the principal
D) The transaction is void

Key Takeaway
When an agent spends his own money while the principal's money is available, Hanafi law treats it as an exchange, not a gift, based on istihsan.

Dismissal of an Agent: Condition of Knowledge and Exceptions
Commentary on the condition of knowledge for effective dismissal and the five exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for effective dismissal of an agent and identify the five exceptions according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Dismissal of an agent is valid only when the agent knows of it — five exceptions confirm this rule.

In the Hanafi school, merely uttering the word of dismissal does not terminate the agency. The principal must ensure the agent becomes aware. This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rule, its exceptions, and related evidentiary rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The author states that agency is invalidated by dismissal only when the agent knows of it. This is the foundational principle.
The rule applies to a wakīl (agent), not a rasūl (messenger).
2
Examine the five exceptions
The text lists five cases where the general rule does not apply: (1) agent for sale of a pledge, (2) agent for litigation at plaintiff's request when principal absent, (3) the weak opinion of reciprocal suspension, (4) agent appointed by court order, and (5) when the agent's own right is attached.
These exceptions demonstrate that the rule is not absolute.
3
Understand evidentiary implications
The passage discusses that evidence of dismissal takes precedence over evidence of sale by the agent. The judge must inquire about the timing of dismissal relative to the agent's actions.
This shows the practical importance of establishing the agent's knowledge.
4
Apply automatic termination
Once the purpose of the agency is achieved (e.g., debt collected, marriage performed), the agency ends automatically without need for dismissal.
This is called 'dismissal without dismissal'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بلفظ العزل لا يصح ا هـ . ثم اعلم أنه لو قال كلما وكلتك فأنت معزول لم يصح، والفرق أن التوكيل يصح تعليقه بالشروط والعزل لا كما صرح به في الصغرى والصيرفية فإذا وكله لم ينعزل .
قوله : ( وتبطل الوكالة بالعزل إذا علم به الوكيل ولو قال كما في المجمع لكان أولى كما قدمناه وأطلق في الوكالة فشمل المنجزة والمعلقة فيملك عزله عن المعلقة قبل وجود الشرط وعليه الفتوى وفي الصغرى وبه يفتى وفي القنية لو قال الوكيل عزلني موكلي وهو غائب وكذبه المدعي لا يقبل قوله. وفي شهادات العتابية وبينة العزل أولى من بينة البيع من الوكيل، وكذا الطلاق والعتاق وإذا شهدوا ببيع الوكيل يجب أن يسألهم القاضي عن بيعه قبل العزل أو بعده، فإن ماتوا أو غابوا قضى بشهادتهم ا.هـ. ولو قال المؤلف «إلا إذا لم يعلم بها فلا يشترط علمه به لكان أولى لما في البزازية : إذا وكله ولم يعلم بها فله عزله وإن لم يعلم به . وقيد بالوكيل لأن عزل الرسول يصح بلا علمه وقدمنا أنه يستثنى من صحة عزله الوكيل ببيع الرهن وبالخصومة بالتماس الطالب عند غيبة الموكل وفيما إذا قال كلما عزلتك فأنت وكيلي على قول ضعيف. ويستثنى ما إذا وكل وكيل البيع موكله بالثمن من المشتري بأمر القاضي فإنه لا يملك إخراجه عنها وأن لا يأمر الحاكم له عزله؛ كذا في البزازية. وما في المحيط. وكله ببيع عين له عزله إلا أن يتعلق به حق الوكيل بأن يأمره بالبيع واستيفاء الثمن بإزاء دينه ا هـ . فالمستثنى خمسة. ثم اعلم أن الوكالة إنما يتوقف بطلانها على العزل إذا لم ينته الأمر، فإن بلغ نهايته العزل بلا عزل كما لو وكله بقبض الدين فقبضه أو بالنكاح فزوجه فإنه ينعزل كما في البزازية
By the word of dismissal it is not valid. Then know that if he said 'Whenever I appoint you, you are dismissed' it is not valid, and the difference is that appointment can be suspended on conditions but dismissal cannot, as stated in al-Sughra and al-Sayrafiyya. So if he appoints him, he is not dismissed. His statement: 'And the agency is invalidated by dismissal when the agent knows of it' – and if he had said 'as in al-Majma'' it would have been better as we previously mentioned. And he made it absolute in agency, so it includes the unconditional and the suspended; thus he has the power to dismiss from the suspended before the condition occurs, and upon this is the fatwa, and in al-Sughra 'and by it fatwa is given.' In al-Qunyah: if the agent says 'my principal dismissed me' while he is absent and the claimant denies it, his statement is not accepted. In Shahadat al-Atabiyyah: the evidence of dismissal takes precedence over the evidence of sale by the agent, and similarly divorce and manumission. If they testify to the agent's sale, the judge must ask them whether it was before or after the dismissal; if they die or are absent, he rules by their testimony. And if the author had said 'except if he did not know of it, then his knowledge is not required' it would have been better, based on al-Bazzaziyyah: if he appoints him and he did not know of it, he has the right to dismiss him even if he did not know of it. And he restricted it to the agent because the dismissal of a messenger is valid without his knowledge. And we have previously stated that there are exceptions to the validity of his dismissal: the agent for sale of a pledge, and the agent for litigation at the request of the plaintiff when the principal is absent, and in the case where he said 'Whenever I dismiss you, you are my agent' – a weak opinion. And there is also excepted the case where the agent for sale appoints his principal over the price from the buyer by order of the judge, for he cannot remove him from it, and the judge should not order his dismissal. And in al-Muhit: if he appoints him to sell a specific item, he has the right to dismiss him unless the right of the agent is attached to it, such as if he orders him to sell and collect the price in lieu of his debt. So the exceptions are five. Then know that the invalidation of the agency depends on dismissal only if the matter has not reached its end; if it reaches its end, it is a dismissal without dismissal, such as if he appointed him to collect a debt and he collected it, or for marriage and he married him off, for he is dismissed as in al-Bazzaziyyah.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the ruling on dismissal of an agent. The author first states that a dismissal expressed by the word 'dismissal' alone is not valid. He then clarifies that a suspended dismissal (e.g., 'Whenever I appoint you, you are dismissed') is also invalid because appointment can be suspended on conditions, but dismissal cannot. The main rule is that agency is invalidated by dismissal only if the agent knows about it. The commentator notes that it would have been better to mention the exception for when the agent does not yet know of the appointment. He lists five exceptions where dismissal is ineffective: (1) the agent for sale of a pledged property, (2) the agent for litigation at the plaintiff's request when the principal is absent, (3) the case of a weak opinion where the principal says 'Whenever I dismiss you, you are my agent', (4) the agent for sale who by court order appoints the principal over the price, and (5) when the agent's own right is attached (e.g., he is to collect the sale price for his own debt). Finally, if the purpose of the agency has been achieved (e.g., debt collected, marriage performed), the agency ends automatically without need for dismissal.

Key Terms
عزل (‘azl): The act of dismissing an agent from his agency by the principal.
وكيل (wakīl): A person appointed by another to act on his behalf in a legal matter.
موكل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if the agent consents

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an agent's dismissal takes effect only when the agent learns of it, with five specific exceptions.

Termination of Agency: Death, Insanity, Apostasy, and Loss of Principal
Commentary on termination triggers and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the events that terminate an agency and distinguish between different types of agency (e.g., binding vs. non-binding) in their effect on termination.

Core Idea
Agency terminates by death, continuous insanity, apostasy, and loss of principal, but exceptions exist for binding agencies like pledge.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies when an agency contract becomes invalid. While the general rule is that agency ends with death, continuous insanity, apostasy, or the loss of the principal, the commentator refines this rule by noting important exceptions, especially for binding agencies. The passage also uncovers a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute on how long continuous insanity must last to terminate the agency—a question with direct practical consequences for the validity of transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terminating events
Read the opening statement to list the four events that invalidate the agency: death of either party, continuous insanity of either, apostasy and joining the enemy, and loss of the principal.
The text uses 'يحقه مرتداً' to mean the agent leaves Islam and joins the enemy (Dar al-Harb).
2
Understand the general rationale
Recognise that agency is a non-binding contract (tasarruf ghayr lazim). Its continuation requires the existence of legal capacity in both parties; the listed events destroy that capacity.
The author states: 'لأن التوكيل تصرف غير لازم فيكون لدوامه حكم ابتدائه فلا بد من قيام الأمر'.
3
Recognise exceptions for specific agencies
Note that the general rule does not apply uniformly. For example, an agent appointed to sell a pledged item is not dismissed by the principal's death or insanity. Similarly, an agent for litigation at the request of the opponent is dismissed, while an agent for divorce is dismissed only by the agent's death (by istihsan).
The passage cites al-Bazzaziyyah and distinguishes between binding (lazim) and non-binding agencies.
4
Analyse the dispute on mutbiq (continuous insanity)
Identify the three positions within the Hanafi school on the required duration: Abu Yusuf says one month (due to fasting), another narration from him says more than a day and night (due to prayers), and Muhammad says one full year (due to all acts of worship).
The text states 'قدره محمد بحول كامل لسقوط جميع العبادات به فقدر به احتياطاً وهو الصحيح'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The commentator declares Muhammad's view (one year) as the correct one. However, later fatwa works may follow Abu Yusuf's one-month view. The practical consequence is that the agency is only terminated when the insanity meets the defined duration; shorter periods do not invalidate it.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the student should be aware of both views and the basis for preferring one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وموت أحدهما وجنونه مطبقاً ولحوقه مرتداً) أي تبطل بهذه الأشياء لأن التوكيل تصرف غير لازم فيكون لدوامه حكم ابتدائه فلا بد من قيام الأمر وقد بطل بهذه العوارض وفي القنية : بلغ المستبضع موت المبضع وهو في الطريق وقد اشترى رقيقاً بمال البضاعة ليس له أن ينفق على الرقيق من بقية مال البضاعة إلا بأمر القاضي وفي التجنيس من باب المفقود: رجل غاب وجعل داراً له في يد رجل ليعمرها فدفع إليه مالاً ليحفظه ثم فقد الدافع فله أن يحفظ، وليس له أن يعمر الدار إلا بإذن الحاكم لأنه لعله قد مات، ولا يكون الرجل وصياً للمفقود حتى يحكم بموته ا هـ. وبهذا علم أن الوكالة تبطل بفقد الموكل في حق التصرف لا الحفظ وظاهر إطلاق المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى أن كل وكالة تبطل بموت الموكل وجنونه وليس كذلك ففي البزازية : قولهم ينعزل بجنون الموكل وموته مقيد بالموضع الذي يملك الموكل عزل وكيله فأما في الرهن فإذا وكل الراهن العدل أو المرتهن الرهن عند حلول الأجل أو الوكيل بالأمر باليد لا ينعزل، وإن مات الموكل أو ببيع جن والوكيل بالخصومة بالتماس الخصم ينعزل بجنون الموكل وموته والوكيل بالطلاق ينعزل بموت الوكيل استحساناً لا قياساً ا هـ .
وعلى هذا يفرق في الوكالة اللازمة بين وكالة ووكالة فالوكالة ببيع الرهن لا تبطل بالعزل حقيقياً أو حكمياً، ولا بالخروج عن الأهلية بالجنون والردة، وفيما عداها من اللازمة. لا تبطل بالحقيقي وتبطل بالحكمي وبالخروج عن الأهلية وقيد بالمطبق لأن قليله بمنزلة الإغماء، وحده شهر عند أبي يوسف اعتباراً بما يسقط به الصوم، وعنه أكثر من يوم وليلة لسقوط الصلوات الخمس فصار كالميت وقدره محمد بحول كامل لسقوط جميع العبادات به فقدر به احتياطاً وهو الصحيح كما ذكره الشارح والمطبق ـ بكسر الباء ـ أي يكون من ذلك. وقيد بالمطبق لأن قليله بمنزلة الإغماء، وحده شهر عند أبي يوسف اعتباراً بما يسقط به الصوم، وعنه أكثر من يوم وليلة لسقوط الصلوات الخمس فصار كالميت وقدره محمد بحول كامل لسقوط جميع العبادات به فقدر به احتياطاً وهو الصحيح كما ذكره الشارح والمطبق ـ بكسر الباء ـ أي يكون من ذلك.
His statement: 'And the death of either of them, his continuous insanity, and his joining as an apostate' meaning it is invalidated by these things because the appointment is a non-binding disposition, so its continuation has the ruling of its initiation, so the matter must exist and it has been invalidated by these accidents. In al-Qunyah: if the recipient of a goods-for-sale knows of the death of the sender while on the road and has purchased slaves with the goods-money, he may not spend on the slaves from the remainder of the goods-money except by order of the judge. In al-Tajnīs, chapter on the lost person: a man disappeared and put his house in the hands of a man to maintain it, and gave him money to preserve it, then the giver was lost. He may preserve it, but he may not maintain the house except with the permission of the judge because perhaps he has died, and the man does not become the executor of the lost person until his death is ruled. From this it is known that agency is invalidated by the loss of the principal in matters of disposition, not preservation. And the apparent generality of the author's statement – may Allah have mercy on him – that every agency is invalidated by death and insanity of the principal is not so, for in al-Bazzaziyyah: their statement 'he is dismissed by the insanity of the principal and his death' is restricted to the case where the principal has the power to dismiss his agent. As for the pledge: if the pledgor appoints the trustee or the pledgee over the pledge at the time of the term, or the agent by order over the hand, he is not dismissed even if the principal dies or becomes insane. And the agent for litigation at the request of the opponent is dismissed by the insanity and death of the principal. And the agent for divorce is dismissed by the death of the agent by istihsan, not by qiyas. Based on this, a distinction is made in binding agency between different types: the agency for sale of a pledge is not invalidated by actual or constructive dismissal, nor by loss of legal capacity due to insanity or apostasy. As for other binding agencies, they are not invalidated by actual dismissal but are invalidated by constructive dismissal and loss of legal capacity. And he restricted it to 'continuous' (mutbiq) because a little of it is like fainting. Its limit is a month according to Abu Yusuf, considering what nullifies fasting; according to another narration from him, more than a day and night because of the dropping of the five prayers, so it becomes like a dead person. Muhammad estimated it as a full year due to all acts of worship being dropped, so he estimated it as a precaution, and it is the correct view as stated by the commentator. And 'mutbiq' (with kasra on the ba) means that it occurs continuously.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the termination of agency. The author explains that agency is invalidated by the death of either the principal or the agent, by continuous insanity of either party, and by the agent's apostasy and joining the enemy. The reason given is that agency is a non-binding contract, so its continuation requires the existence of the legal capacity of both parties. The text then provides examples from al-Qunyah and al-Tajnīs regarding the loss of the principal (fqd): if the principal is lost, the agent can preserve property but cannot perform acts of disposition without court permission, because the principal may be dead. The commentator clarifies that the generality of the rule does not apply to all cases; for instance, in the case of a pledge (rahn), the agent appointed by the pledgor is not dismissed by the principal's death or insanity. Similarly, the agent for litigation at the request of the opponent is dismissed, while the agent for divorce is dismissed by the agent's death by istihsan (juristic preference), not by qiyas (analogy). The passage then discusses the duration of 'mutbiq' (continuous insanity) that terminates agency. Abu Yusuf defined it as one month (because it nullifies fasting), another narration from him says more than a day and night (because it nullifies prayers), and Muhammad said a full year (because all acts of worship are dropped). The commentator states that the correct view is Muhammad's, as a precaution. This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf has practical consequences: the agency terminates only when the insanity reaches the defined duration.

Key Terms
مطبق (muṭbiq): Continuous insanity that lasts for a defined period (one month or one year according to different views) such that it terminates the agency.
لحوق مرتداً (luḥūq murtaddan): The agent's apostasy and joining the enemy (i.e., leaving Islam and going to Dar al-Harb), which terminates the agency.
فقد (faqd): The state of being lost or missing (i.e., the principal's whereabouts unknown), which terminates the agency only with respect to acts of disposition, not preservation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following does NOT terminate a regular (non-binding) agency?
A) Death of the agent
B) The principal becoming temporarily unconscious for a day
C) The agent apostatising and joining the enemy
D) The principal being lost (fqd) with unknown whereabouts

Key Takeaway
Agency terminates by death, continuous insanity (of defined duration), apostasy, and loss of principal (for disposition only), but binding agencies like pledge sales are exceptions.

8 min
Creditor Self-Help: Same Genus Condition and Disputes
Inter-madhhab dispute on creditor self-help

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for creditor self-help, explain the Shafi'i counter-position, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with the muftā bihi.

Core Idea
A creditor may take only property of the same genus (jins) and quality without court.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq addresses a critical financial fiqh issue: can a creditor take the debtor’s property without going to court? The Hanafi school lays down strict conditions – only property of the same genus and quality may be taken. Imam al-Shāfi‘ī disagrees, and even within the Hanafi school there is a divergence on a third party’s role. Understanding these rulings is essential for applying fiqh to debt recovery scenarios.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The creditor may take from the debtor's property only if it is of the same genus (jins) and quality as the debt (e.g., dirhams for dirhams).
This is the general rule from the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Imam al-Shāfi‘ī holds that the creditor may take any property up to the value of the debt, regardless of genus.
This is a clear inter-madhhab dispute.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Bakr al-Rāzī permits taking a different type (e.g., dinars for dirhams) by istihsān, but this is a minority view. Also, on the third-party helper: Ibn Salamah says both the third party and debtor are usurpers, while Nasīr ibn Yahyā says the third party is not liable and is merely a helper – this latter view is relied upon.
The text gives two intra-Hanafi opinions.
4
Determine the muftā bihi
The relied-upon (muftā bihi) position is that the third party is not a usurper and is not liable; he is a helper. The same-genus condition remains the mainstream Hanafi view.
The text says 'wa bihi yuftā' after Nasīr's view.
5
Apply to a scenario
Suppose a creditor is owed 100 dirhams. He finds a gold necklace worth 100 dirhams in the debtor's house. Under Hanafi, he may not take it because it is a different genus. Under Shāfi‘ī, he may take it. If a friend takes the necklace and gives it to the creditor, the friend is not a usurper per muftā bihi.
This shows the practical thamarah al-khilāf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان ديناً ففي مداينات القنية : رب الدين إذا ظفر من جنس حقه من مال المديون على صفته فله أخذه بغير رضاه ولا يأخذ خلاف جنسه كالدراهم والدنانير، وعند الشافعي له أخذه بقدر قيمته، وعن أبي بكر الرازي له أخذ الدنانير بالدراهم، وكذا أخذ الدراهم بالدنانير استحساناً قياساً. ولو أخذ من الغريم غيره ودفعه إلى الدائن قال ابن سلمة : هو والغريم غاصب، فإن قصاصاً بدينه، وإن ضمن الغريم صار قصاصاً. وقال نصير بن يحيى : ضمن الآخذ لم يصر صار قصاصاً بدينه والآخذ معين له و به يفتي . ولو غصب جنس الدين من المديون فغصبه منه المديون فالمختار هنا قول ابن سلمة ا.هـ. وظاهر قول أصحابنا أن له الأخذ من جنسه مقراً كان أو منكراً، له بينة أو لا، ولم أر حكم ما إذا لم يتوصل إليه إلا بكسر الباب ونقب الجدار وينبغي أن له ذلك حيث لا يمكنه الأخذ بالحاكم، وإذا أخذ غير الجنس بغير إذنه فتلف في يده ضمنه ضمان الرهن كما في غصب البزازية، ولم أر حكم ما إذا ظفر بمال مديون مديونه والجنس واحد فيهما، وينبغي أن يجوز الثامن في دليلها الكتاب والسنة والإجماع وهي شهيرة. والتاسع في أنواعها العاشر في وجوده دفعها وسيأتيان . قوله : (ولو أخذ من الغريم غيره أي أخذ جنس الحق من الغريم غير رب الدين ودفعه لرب الدين قوله : قال ابن سلمة هو والغريم (غاصب) عبارة القنية هو غاصب والغريم غاصب الغاصب قوله : (ولو غصب جنس الدين من المديون فغصبه منه المديون (الخ) كذا في النسخ والذي في القنية
If it is a debt, then in Mudayanat of al-Quniyya: The creditor, if he finds from the debtor's property something of the same genus as his right and same quality, he may take it without his consent. He may not take something of a different genus like dirhams and dinars. According to al-Shafi'i, he may take it up to its value. And from Abu Bakr al-Razi, he may take dinars for dirhams, and similarly take dirhams for dinars by istihsan (juristic preference) and qiyas (analogy). If someone other than the creditor takes from the debtor and gives it to the creditor, Ibn Salamah said: He and the debtor are both usurpers (ghasib); if it is offset (qisas) against the debt, and if the debtor guarantees (the taken property), it becomes offset. Nasir ibn Yahya said: The taker is not liable, it becomes offset against the debt, and the taker is his helper; and this is the fatwa. If someone usurps the same genus of the debt from the debtor, then the debtor usurps it from him, the preferred view here is the statement of Ibn Salamah, etc. The apparent position of our companions is that he may take from the same genus whether the debtor admits or denies, whether he has a witness or not. I did not see a ruling if he cannot reach it except by breaking the door or digging a wall; it should be that he may do so where he cannot take through the judge. If he takes something of a different genus without permission and it is lost in his hand, he is liable with the liability of a pledge (damān al-rahn) as in Ghasp al-Bazzaziyya. I did not see a ruling if he finds property of the debtor's debtor and the genus is the same for both; it should be permissible. The eighth (proof) is the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma', which are well-known. The ninth is about its types, the tenth about its existence; its refusal will come later. His saying: (And if someone takes from the debtor something else) i.e., takes the same genus of the right from the debtor other than the creditor and gives it to the creditor. His saying: Ibn Salamah said: He and the debtor are usurpers; the expression of al-Quniyya is: He is a usurper and the debtor is the usurper of the usurper. His saying: (And if he usurps the same genus of the debt from the debtor, and the debtor usurps it from him) etc. Thus in the copies, and what is in al-Quniyya...
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage deals with the creditor's right to take his debt without court order. The Hanafi ruling is that the creditor may only take property of the same type (jins) and quality as the debt. Imam al-Shafi'i allows taking any property up to the value. Within the Hanafi school, Abu Bakr al-Razi permits taking a different type of currency (e.g., dinars for dirhams) by istihsan. The passage also discusses a scenario where a third party takes the debt from the debtor and gives it to the creditor: Ibn Salamah says both the third party and debtor are usurpers, and if the debtor guarantees, it becomes offset. Nasir ibn Yahya says the third party is not liable; he is merely a helper, and this is the mufta bihi view. The author also adds his own opinions on breaking down doors, liability for different genus taken without permission, and taking from a sub-debtor. The final lines reference proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma.

Key Terms
دين (dayn): Debt, an obligation of monetary value.
جنس (jins): Genus, type, category (e.g., dirhams, dinars).
قصاص (qisas): Here used in the sense of offsetting a debt, not retaliation.
إستحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of reasoning in Hanafi fiqh.
غاصب (ghasib): Usurper, one who wrongfully takes another's property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The third party is a usurper together with the debtor.
B) The third party is not liable and is a helper of the creditor.
C) The third party becomes the debtor.
D) The third party must have the debtor's permission.

Key Takeaway
A creditor may take only property of the same genus (jins) as the debt without court permission; the third-party helper is not a usurper per the muftā bihi.

Identifying the Proper Opponent in Property Claims
Rulings on proper opponent in various property claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the proper opponent in claims involving lease, sale, gift, mortgage, usurpation, deposit, option sale, and void purchase, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the necessity of the claimant's presence in the offspring case.

Core Idea
The proper opponent varies by transaction and possession – a lessee is not always the opponent, and a usurper can be sued even without possession.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies who is the correct defendant (khasm) when property claims arise. In Hanafi litigation procedure, suing the wrong party wastes time and may invalidate the claim. The author presents specific rulings for leases, sales, mortgages, usurpation, deposits, and option contracts, concluding with a debated point about claiming offspring.

Guided Path
1
Lessee and Buyer/Donee
Identify the ruling for the lessee: he is the opponent for a claim of lease in the owner's absence (preferred view), but according to the sound view, he is not the opponent for claims of lease, mortgage, or purchase. The buyer and donee are opponents for all claims.
The lessee's role is limited; the buyer is a universal opponent.
2
Mortgage Claim
For a claim regarding a mortgaged object, the presence of both the mortgagor and mortgagee is required for the claim to be valid.
Both parties are necessary because the mortgage involves a contractual relationship between them.
3
Usurper and Depositary
A usurper can be sued even if the object is not in his possession. The rightful owner may sue the seller alone because the buyer is considered a usurper. A depositary or usurper who acknowledges the deposit or usurpation is not an opponent for the buyer but is an opponent for the heir of the depositor or the person wronged.
The key is whether the possessor acknowledges the claim; acknowledgment changes the opponent.
4
Option Sale and Void Buyer
If someone buys with an option (khiyar) and a third party claims the property, both seller and buyer must be present. A void buyer (purchase invalid) is not an opponent for the rightful owner – the claim must be against the seller.
The option contract gives both parties a stake; a void purchase does not create a valid opponent.
5
Dispute on Offspring Claim
When a sold animal's offspring is claimed after judgment, the seller may prove the offspring to avoid recourse for the price. Scholars differed: the correct view (الأصح) is that the presence of the claimant is not required; some said it is required (المختار).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf where the later preferred view (mufta bihi) is that presence is not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمستأجر خصم لمن يدعي الإجارة في غيبة المالك على الأقرب إلى الصواب وليس بخصم على الصحيح لمن يدعي الإجارة أو الرهن أو الشراء، والمشتري خصم للكل كالموهوب له وفي دعوى العين المرهونة تشترط حضرة الراهن والمرتهن وتصح الدعوى على الغاصب وإن لم تكن العين في يده فلذا كان للمستحق الدعوى على البائع وحده وإن كان المبيع في يد المشتري لكونه غاصباً، والمودع أو الغاصب إذا كان مقراً بالوديعة أو الغصب لا ينتصب خصماً للمشتري وينتصب لوارث المودع أو المغصوب منه ومن اشترى شيئاً بالخيار فادعاه آخر يشترط حضرة البائع والمشتري والمشتري باطلاً لا يكون خصماً للمستحق، وإذا استحق المبيع بالملك المطلق وقضى به فبرهن البائع على النتاج وبرهن على المشتري في غيبة المستحق ليدفع عنه الرجوع بالثمن اختلف المشايخ فيه والأصح أنه لا تشترط حضرته ومنهم من قال : المختار اشتراطها .
And the lessee is the opponent for one who claims a lease in the absence of the owner, according to the closest to correctness, but he is not the opponent, according to the sound view, for one who claims a lease, mortgage, or purchase. And the buyer is the opponent for all, like the donee. And in a claim regarding a mortgaged object, the presence of the mortgagor and mortgagee is required. And a claim against a usurper is valid even if the object is not in his hand; therefore, the rightful owner may sue the seller alone even if the sold object is in the buyer's hand because he is a usurper. The depositary or usurper, if they acknowledge the deposit or usurpation, do not become opponents for the buyer, but they become opponents for the heir of the depositor or the person from whom the object was usurped. And if someone buys something with an option and another claims it, the presence of the seller and buyer is required. And a void buyer is not an opponent for the rightful owner. And if the sold object is claimed through absolute ownership and judgment is given, and then the seller proves the offspring and the buyer proves [something] in the absence of the rightful claimant to repel recourse for the price, the scholars differed. The correct view is that his presence is not required, and some said the chosen view is that it is required.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage details various scenarios regarding who is the proper opponent (خصم) in different claims. For lease claims in the owner's absence, the lessee is considered the opponent according to the preferred view (على الأقرب إلى الصواب), but the sound view (على الصحيح) is that the lessee is not the opponent for a claim of lease, mortgage, or purchase. The buyer is the opponent for all claims, like the donee. For a mortgaged property, both mortgagor and mortgagee must be present. A usurper can be sued even if the property is not in his possession; thus, if the rightful owner sues the seller when the property is with the buyer, it is valid because the buyer is considered a usurper. If a depositary or usurper acknowledges the deposit or usurpation, they are not the opponent for the buyer but are for the heir. For a sale with an option, both seller and buyer must be present when a third party claims the property. A void buyer is not an opponent. Finally, there is a specific case and a difference of opinion regarding the necessity of the presence of the claimant when the seller proves offspring. The correct view (الأصح) is that his presence is not required, but some say the chosen view (المختار) is that it is required.

Key Terms
مستأجر (musta'jir): Lessee or tenant
مشتري (mushtari): Buyer
موهوب له (mawhub lahu): Donee (recipient of a gift)
راهن (rahin): Mortgagor (one who pledges property as collateral)
مرتهن (murtahin): Mortgagee (one who receives the pledge)
غاصب (ghasib): Usurper (one who wrongfully takes or holds property)
مودع (mudi'): Depositary (one with whom something is deposited)
خيار (khiyar): Option (right to rescind a contract)
مشتري باطلاً (mushtari batilan): Void buyer (a purchase that is invalid)
نتاج (nataj): Offspring (of a sold animal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, who is the proper opponent for a claim regarding a mortgaged object?
A) The mortgagor alone
B) The mortgagee alone
C) Both mortgagor and mortgagee together
D) The court-appointed representative

Key Takeaway
The proper opponent in property claims depends on the type of transaction and possession; always verify the specific ruling before initiating a lawsuit.

Inclusion of Boundaries in Sale: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on boundary inclusion in sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on boundaries in sale and explain the thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Mentioning boundaries in a sale is descriptive unless explicitly saying 'with its boundaries'.

When selling a property, sellers often mention boundaries like a river or road. Does including such boundaries in the contract mean they are sold with the property? Abu Hanifa and his student Abu Yusuf disagreed on this point. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and shows how a simple phrase 'bihududihi' resolves the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and dispute
What is the legal act? A sale contract where boundaries are written. Who disagrees and on what specific point?
Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf within the Hanafi school.
2
State each position and its ruling
Abu Hanifa rules the sale valid, boundaries not sold. Abu Yusuf rules the sale invalid because boundaries are part of the property.
Hukm level: sahih vs fasid.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil) for each
Abu Hanifa relies on custom (urf): people mention boundaries to identify, not to include. Abu Yusuf argues that boundaries physically touch the property and ambiguity invalidates.
Each uses talil (reasoning) about intent.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: if boundaries are mentioned, sale valid per Abu Hanifa, invalid per Abu Yusuf. If 'bihududihi' is added, both agree boundaries are included.
The phrase removes ambiguity.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The author says 'ikhtarna' (we choose) Abu Hanifa's view, so the relied-upon fatwa is that sale is valid and boundaries are not sold unless explicitly stated.
Zahir al-Riwayah supports Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو يلاصق كذا أو لزيق كذا ولا يكتب أحد حدوده كذا. وقال أبو حنيفة : لو كتب أحد حدوده دجلة أو الطريق أو المسجد فالبيع جائز ولا تدخل الحدود في البيع إذ قصد الناس به إظهار ما يقع عليه البيع لكن قال أبو يوسف البيع فاسد إذ الحدود فيه تدخل في البيع أو لزيق أو يلاصق تحرزاً عن الخلاف، ولأن الدار على قول من يقول يدخل في البيع هي الموضع الذي ينتهي إليه فأما ذلك الموضع المنتهي إليه فقد جعل حداً وهو داخل في البيع وعلى قول من يقول لا يدخل الحد في البيع فالمنتهي إلى الدار لا يدخل تحت البيع ولكن عند ذكر قولنا بحدوده يدخل في المبيع وفاقاً ا هـ.
Or adjacent like this, or adjacent like this, and one does not write any of its boundaries like this. Abu Hanifa said: If one writes its boundaries as the Tigris, or the road, or the mosque, the sale is valid and the boundaries are not included in the sale, because people intend by that to show what the sale falls upon. But Abu Yusuf said: The sale is invalid because the boundaries are included in the sale, or adjacent or attached, to avoid disagreement, and because the house according to the one who says the boundary enters the sale is the place that ends at it. As for that place that ends at it, it has been made a boundary and it is included in the sale. According to the one who says the boundary does not enter the sale, what ends at the house does not come under the sale. But when we say 'with its boundaries', it enters the sold item in agreement. Ends.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the effect of specifying boundaries in a sale contract. Abu Hanifa holds that when a seller writes boundaries such as a river, road, or mosque, the sale is valid and the boundaries themselves are not included in the sale; they are merely descriptive to identify the property. Abu Yusuf argues that the sale is invalid because such boundaries are part of the sold property, and not including them creates ambiguity. The author notes that if the contract explicitly says 'with its boundaries', then the boundaries are included by agreement. This is an example of talil (legal reasoning) based on the intent of the parties and the nature of boundaries.

Key Terms
حدود (hudud): Boundaries of a property mentioned in a sale contract.
بحدوده (bihududihi): A phrase meaning 'with its boundaries', indicating the boundaries are included in the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a sale contract mentions the boundaries without the phrase 'bihududihi'?
A) The sale is invalid because the boundaries create ambiguity.
B) The sale is valid and the boundaries are included.
C) The sale is valid and the boundaries are not included.
D) The sale is voidable at the option of the buyer.

Key Takeaway
When boundaries are mentioned in a sale without 'bihududihi', they serve only to identify the property and are not part of the sold items, per the relied-upon Hanafi view.
